​[ ​4​ ]​

AI RESOURCES FOR WRITERS

Since I encourage you to try out the tools and methods I discuss actively, let me introduce the ones I’m familiar with. Of course, you are not limited to this list, and with the warp speed that AI is developing, new ones will soon appear.

Tools

1. OpenAI ChatGPT ⁠1 This is the granddaddy of all AI chatbots because it is my first experience with AI. ChatGPT is my go-to AI buddy trained on everything its creators could get their hands on: public domain text, internet archives, fan fiction, chatrooms, tons of code and formulas, and more. It was an experimental generative AI tool made for research purposes, and hence, the training can seem haphazard. It is the jack-of-all-trades chatbot based on OpenAI’s generations of GPT LLMs.

2. OpenAI Playground ⁠2 and API. The playground is OpenAI’s developer’s interface, allowing them to try out prompts and responses without writing code. The playground will enable users to tweak parameters to adjust how the LLM responds to your prompt (input). You can try out various generations of GPTs with the Playground. OpenAI has also allowed users to fine-tune their models to produce outputs skewed in a particular fashion or style. This in itself is exciting to creative writers. It eliminates the “generic” sound of AI-generated text and allows authors to shape their voice and tone to write more like themselves.

3. Anthropic’s Claude ⁠3 This LLM was developed by Anthropic, a different organization, and has its own characteristics. By happy accident, the fiction writers I know find Claude a “better writer.” Of course, this is highly subjective, and ChatGPT is still a favorite all-around brainstormer, idea generator, and structure generator; the feeling is that Claude writes better prose. However, Claude is also smart and good at analysis, and coders claim it is excellent at code generation. As you’ll see, any model’s responses are heavily influenced by your prompting.

4. Claude API. As of March 2024, Anthropic opened the Claude API to every subscriber. Anthropic has its own Playground analogue called Workbench. ⁠4

5. Google Gemini LLM ⁠5 Google is the search engine; hence, one of Gemini’s strengths is its ability to find reference material on the Internet. Currently, Google allows access to its Gemini Pro 1.5 model in the Google AI Studio ⁠6. This model has a large context window (1,000,000 tokens) and allows users to upload documents, images, and videos. After uploading, you can ask questions about the content, which is helpful for story creation and developmental editing.

6. Sudowrite ⁠7 This comprehensive AI writing application wraps the underlying AI with a graphical user interface that provides step-by-step paths for story development and prose generation. There are other tools like Novelcrafter, but Sudowrite is the one I am familiar with. I detailed my use of Sudowrite in writing a complete novel in An AI Author’s Journal: From 0 to 70000 in 14 Days. ⁠8

7. Future Fiction Academy ⁠9 - Rexy ⁠10. Ah, how do I describe Rexy? It is a sequencing tool available to members of the Future Fiction Academy that is intermediate between a developer’s playground and a user-friendly application. It is the brainchild of the founders of Future Fiction Academy, Elizabeth Ann West, Stephanie Pajonas, and Leeland Atra, and one designed for writers to customize their AI prompts and responses. Rexy has a web-based graphical user interface that connects the user to a data store and their personal notion pages and then passes information along with user-defined prompts to the LLMs they support. It is transparent and allows users to pick and choose their AI model and parameters and customize the prompts to fit their workflow. The goal of the FFA is to push the envelope of using AI for fiction writing and provide accessibility to the latest AI methodology to the ordinary author. The Future Fiction Academy leads the research into using AI for fiction writing.

8. Other “bring your own LLM API” tools include Typing Mind ⁠11, Rexy, and Novelcrafter ⁠12. While 2023 was the year of ChatGPT and kitchen sink LLMs, 2024 is the proliferation of LLMs out of the wazoo. The huggingface.co ⁠13 community is an attempt to keep up with a catalog of LLMs.

9. LLM Aggregators. Many places now offer ways for users to pay for API access to an LLM through aggregators like Openrouter.ai Playground ⁠14, Poe.com ⁠15, or Hugging Chat ⁠16. Users can select from the many LLMs offered, and the aggregator will pass on the payment. These include open-source LLMs and ones that are unfiltered, allowing violence and sex. The Future Fiction Academy’s Rexy supports all the LLMs included on Openrouter.ai and even integrates with OpenAI’s fine-tuned models, thus allowing a high degree of customization.

10. Autocrit - started many years ago primarily as a critiquing tool to look at overused words, slow pacing, and features many other bells and whistles. However, in the last year, they’ve been actively incorporating gen-AI into their suite of tools, making it capable of ideation and story concept, story development of characters, settings, and plot points (in their Inspiration Studio), and developmental editing with its Story Analyzer. ⁠17 Autocrit can also help discovery writers by suggesting the following scenes in many different ways with its “What Happens Next” feature and using “Mood Changer” to change the tone of a scene.

11. ProwritingAid—This program polishes manuscripts, looking for overused words and grammatical mistakes. It has recently incorporated generative AI to suggest alternate phrasing, change tenses and mood, and continue writing in different ways, such as adding a counterargument, joke, or quote.

12. Grammarly Pro - primarily a grammar checker, but lately, it has incorporated generative AI to suggest rewrites or expand on existing text.

​[ ​PART 2​ ]​

THE ROLE OF AI IN FICTION

​[ ​5​ ]​

HOW AI FITS INTO THE FICTION WRITING PROCESS

Now that we understand how generative AI works, let’s look at how we can use these LLM beasties in our fiction writing process. It’s important to acknowledge that every individual writer has his own writing process, and what works for one author may not work for another.

Some of you are planners who map out your stories to the last detail before writing a single word, whereas others write into the wind and let inspiration take the story where it will go. The beauty is that everyone’s creative process is as unique as their fingerprint. And guess what?

AI can fit into your process or style and meet you no matter where you are. There is no definitive approach to using AI—it’s all about what suits you best. The important thing is to be adaptable and open-minded in how AI tools and techniques can be used. AI’s role in your writing can be as flexible and personalized as you make it.

We will break down the way fiction authors use AI into several phases. Even though these phases are listed in a particular order, it does not mean your writing process flows the same way. Some of you might skip the planning phase and rough draft without an outline, only to go back later and add story structure. Others write best with a detailed roadmap accompanied by clearly defined character sketches and rich world-building.

AI can be integrated into your process and accessed at any storytelling stage. Some of you are dying to jump ahead into the tools and advanced techniques section, and that’s okay, too. Check out the technology, and then come back and decide where AI fits into your writing process. Or read straight through to understand the possibilities and try the methods I describe as you go.

​[ ​6​ ]​

STORY CONCEPT AND IDEATION

AI can help during the exploration and creativity stage of a story concept. This phase involves developing creative ideas and fleshing out the essential elements that will form the story’s foundation. Ideation is crucial as it sets the direction and tone for the work that follows.

Authors often start by brainstorming ideas to come up with unique concepts and evaluate how they fit into the overall story idea. This is crucial for genre fiction authors because readers have specific expectations for each type of story.

AI can take your ideas and make connections between them and other concepts in your genre. Using AI’s vast training data, you can identify opportunities, clarify your market niche, and develop ideas based on current trends.

You can use AI’s insights to define your ideal reader and glean what would delight or challenge them. If you decide to be different, AI can invent wild twists to subvert or reinvent genre conventions and ensure your story stands out in the market.

Here’s a breakdown of what typically happens during the concept and ideation phase in writing:

Market Analysis: Choosing a genre or sub-genre of interest and analyzing the concepts and content resonating in the market. Analyzing the book descriptions of top books in the category and looking for trends, fit, and target audience.

Premise Generation: Brainstorm or generate a variety of ideas that fit into your chosen niche: genre, sub-genre, trope, and other characteristics. Be as detailed as possible. Ask for unique twists. Be conversational and refine your prompts.

Research: Conducting preliminary research is often part of concept development. You can use AI or a search engine to look into existing literature, historical events, scientific concepts, or cultural trends to find inspiration or ensure the originality and feasibility of their ideas. Leverage generative AI’s ability to “make things up” by asking it to come up with something different or surprising from the data you gathered.

Audience Analysis: Use AI to create avatars of your likely readers, defining their characteristics, needs, and what they hope to get from your book. Later, use AI to analyze your manuscript to see how you satisfied each avatar’s desires.

Concept Development: Create or consider possible titles, subtitles, log lines, synopsis, blurbs, and hook/pitch combinations.

Validation: This step involves evaluating the viability and appeal of the ideas. Writers might consider factors like market trends, potential audience, and personal interest or expertise to decide which ideas are worth pursuing. AI can give additional insights on the fit and framing of your story idea.

Pitching: In professional settings, be prepared to pitch the developed ideas to editors, publishers, or collaborators to gauge interest and receive feedback, which can further refine the concept before moving into detailed planning and writing. AI can give you the bullet points and prioritize the appeal of your ideas to a particular audience.

Rapid Iteration: The speed and flexibility of AI-powered brainstorming allow writers to generate and test a high volume of ideas in a short amount of time. By quickly exploring multiple angles and possibilities, you can hone in on the most promising concepts and make informed decisions about which direction to take your story.

TOOLS AND TECHNIQUES FOR STORY CONCEPT AND IDEATION

The chatbot is king and queen in this phase. They are easy to use and conversational, allowing you to go from general to specific as you add more detail or branch off tangents.

Choose the “smartest” one you can access because they possess larger training datasets and abilities to connect disparate ideas in unique and surprising ways. Whereas the smaller or earlier chatbot might go for the most obvious ideas, giving you clichéd premises and repetitive concepts, the larger models can draw connections between seemingly unrelated areas and help to generate fresh, innovative story ideas.

Try different chatbots for a broader spectrum of insight and advice. ChatGPT is the obvious starting point, but Anthropic’s Claude, Microsoft Copilot, Google Gemini, Meta’s Llama, Mistral, etc. These versatile chatbots can be used for brainstorming, generating ideas, and exploring different narrative possibilities through conversation.

Prompt Engineering/Design will give you the most bang for the buck at this stage, as chatbots converse with you through your inputs, called prompts.

Specific techniques that will improve your results include iterative prompting, role-based prompting, and prompt chaining. Because each chatbot is different, a good practice is to ask the chatbot what information it needs from you to perform a particular task. Definitions are also important, so ask the chatbot what it thinks a particular word or concept means to find common ground for conversation.

Overall, ideation is about creating a fertile ground from which a detailed and engaging narrative can grow. It’s a phase that requires creativity, insight, and strategic thinking, which can be enhanced using AI tools to produce more informed and compelling content ideas.

​[ ​7​ ]​

STORY DEVELOPMENT: FROM PREMISE TO PLOT

Now that you have the initial premise and concept for your story, it’s time to plan and grow it into a compelling story with all the moving parts, such as a vivid story world, memorable and invigorating characters, and a plot that propels the characters through memorable and exciting plot points.

AI can help with all these stages and provide alternate insights and additional what-ifs for your consideration. If you’re writing genre fiction, now is the time to check that genre expectations are met while throwing in your own twists or blending of genres. The LLMs can assist you by making suggestions, but you are the glue that decides what sticks and which plot twists, themes, or hallmark moments to include.

Even though I document these as steps, please remember to fit the AI and the steps to your individual writing process and not the other way around. Some of you may skip this stage entirely, run off to drafting, and circle back to flesh out your characters or settings during revision.

Personalize your use of AI tools and use them as you desire. Whether you’re a meticulous planner or a seat-of-the-pants discovery writer, AI can assist or entertain you with its insights.

Here is the breakdown of what typically happens during the story development phase.

Expand Premise into Synopsis: Try various synopsis proposals and run them through AI to check genre conventions and expectations. Suggest various twists, tropes, and themes and ask the LLM to craft a synopsis with these variations. Include any genre-specific tropes you want to use, such as doppelganger for horror or betrayal in a buddy romance. Or have AI suggest some and then test them out. Ask another LLM to evaluate the synopsis until you are satisfied. You can also utilize AI tools to research popular tropes, themes, and plot structures within your genre.

Note: I find it useful to iteratively develop my characters as I refine my premise and synopsis. After all, each character’s goals and motivations, flaws, and strengths have much to do with the story’s premise and synopsis. See Chapter 44: Story Development Using ChatGPT.

Crafting Compelling Characters: Chatting with AI is a wonderful way of fleshing out your characters. Whether you use character sheets (template-based prompting) or conversation (iterative prompting), you can discuss with AI the details such as background, strengths, weaknesses, motivations, and other characteristics of your characters. Remember, you can put in your vision of the characters and use AI for additional insights. You do not have to take what AI gives you. Go back and forth between characters and premise until you have a sense of conflicts, opposing characters, sidekicks and allies, and other genre-specific constraints. For a romance, design a hero who will bring out your heroine’s best and worst characteristics. For romantic suspense, don’t forget a villain with personal motives that make him/her scarier. Put your heart and soul into your characters, and then ask AI to evaluate the character arc and see if you’re missing anything.

AI can also suggest other character archetypes and traits to explore or perhaps assign a Myers-Briggs personality type to the character you describe. Tag team with AI to delve into your character’s backstory and defining moment when their mistaken belief took root. Explore what success looks like for your characters.

You can even upload photos and ask AI to describe your characters physically or use AI to suggest a dialogue style for your character, such as how they speak, along with their personality quirks. The possibilities are endless. I used ChatGPT Plus with Dall-E to generate images of wedding dresses so I could visualize them and then asked AI to describe them. We even did one that looked like toilet paper rolls just for laughs.

Building Your Story World and Setting: Here, you can use AI’s universe of knowledge and work together to generate the perfect setting or story world. You can use template prompting or chain-of-thought where you progressively go into more detail about each aspect of the story world. If your story world needs magic, rules, or an invented language, AI can help you create these elements. Use follow-up prompting to explore aspects like history, geography, cultural traditions, mythology, and anything else you need. Work with a multimodal LLM to generate images that can inspire you or document locations and settings. If you need a map, you can sketch it out on a piece of notebook paper and upload it to an image generator that can prettify it and make it look like it’s drawn on parchment or a computer screen by using words to describe how you want the map to appear.

Plan the Story Structure: While AI can suggest plot points and create an outline for you, a better way might be for you to decide on a story structure that fits your vision and the genre-specific content ahead of time. Earlier LLMs will usually generate a “hero’s journey-like” structure. This is true even if you ask for another structure, such as Save the Cat or Romancing the Beat. It doesn’t have as much knowledge of these structures since they are more recent and have less literature about them, but many times, the LLM will happily declare that it knows the structure you propose and generate something it believes matches that structure. This is a situation where it’s better to “train” the LLM on what you want it to do. Give it the structure you want it to use, either in the form of a template or as an explanation of the steps, and then ask it to generate an outline. As I mentioned before, one way to do this is to define a four-act structure and tell it the genre-specific beats you expect. Then, ask the LLM to fill in that structure with the information you developed: premise, synopsis, characters, setting, trope, must-have scenes, etc.

Developing Your Plot and Outline: Now that you have all the information you need, you can work with the LLM to create an outline specific to your story. Do you see that all the preparation was necessary to craft a non-generic outline? By layering the prompts and compiling your story-specific requirements, you add your vision and creativity into the process to tailor the output to your individuality. Of course, you can iterate and fix up the outline, adding and deleting, or even asking for alternate endings. The beauty of using AI is that you can do rapid prototyping and analysis by asking the LLM to critique the outline or compare it with the proposed genre or your target audience’s desires. AI can also offer suggestions to improve the pacing and escalating tension, as well as ensure your outline captures all crucial plot developments and turning points. It can evaluate whether you have too many action scenes, enough cliffhangers, or anything else you wish to analyze. You can “story doctor” the outline rather than wait until you have a first draft to do development editing.

TOOLS AND TECHNIQUES FOR STORY DEVELOPMENT

Chat Interface: The chatbot is again your first go-to for iteratively expanding and refining your story concept. However, as you go, you will want to collect your outputs into a file and tag it as Story Information with sections for Hook, Pitch, Synopsis, Main Characters, Setting, Plot Points, and Outline. Keep this file offline so you don’t lose it in the chatbot. You will use it later as input to either chats or LLMs that work through APIs (Application Programming Interfaces) or Playgrounds (Workbenches).

Custom GPTs: OpenAI allows users with a paid account to create Custom GPTs with additional pre-seeded instructions and a knowledge base. This provides additional context and guidelines for the model to generate domain-specific instructions. These custom GPTs can be very useful if you are writing genre fiction.

For example, I created one called Romance Writing Coach (https://chat.openai.com/g/g-WFzdoMZvY-romance-writing-coach) ⁠1 by uploading information about tropes, romantic tension, likable character traits, four-act romance structure, and a writing style that engages romance readers. When approaching a Custom GPT, the best thing you can do is ask it questions, and it will tell you how it can help you.

Specialized Fiction-Writing Apps and Websites: Prepackaged fiction writing tools such as Sudowrite and Novelcrafter provide a framework within which users can develop their story, including writing with AI. The degree of control or lack thereof depends on whether the tool is writing the prompt for you or you are passing your prompt through the tool to the underlying LLMs. The Future Fiction Academy ⁠2 provides a prompt chaining and sequencing tool with complete flexibility through Rexy. This specialized writing tool is transparent because you can log the exact prompts it generates and pass them to the LLM. It also allows the user to select LLMs, tweak parameters, use megaprompting techniques, and sequence prompts automatically.

Visualization and Image tools: OpenAI’s Dall-E ⁠3 image generator is integrated into ChatGPT Plus. Adobe’s Firefly ⁠4 allows you to upload and refine a sketch by describing the changes you want. Midjourney ⁠5 is one of the most versatile text-to-image generators.

By utilizing a diverse toolkit of AI apps and techniques, you can accelerate and enhance the planning phase of your story development. Here is an example of using AI to visualize wedding gowns.

<Prompt>

Dall-E: please visualize this wedding gown. The third dress featured a weird toilet paper cozy-looking ruffle situation that belonged on a craft project, not a wedding gown.

</Prompt>

<Response>

</Response>

As the storyteller, you are responsible for asking the right questions and guiding the AI with your vision for the story. While it’s interesting to see what the AI can generate from a minimal prompt, the story becomes yours when you add your opinions and detailed follow-up questions. So feel free to chat and explore the serendipity of brainstorming with another mind or multiple minds. Layer in your individuality to make the story truly yours.

​[ ​8​ ]​

WRITING AND REFINING

Now that you’ve done your prep work, it’s time to roll up your sleeves and start writing that first draft. Your AI assistant is here to help, whether you use it to refine your text, suggest refinements and transitions, or write that dirty first draft. It’s your choice where you draw the boundaries, whether you only use AI to rewrite your text or you use it to generate the words of your manuscript. It is only an assistant, whether used as a fancy thesaurus or as a ghostwriter. It can help you with descriptions and dialogue or fill the blank page with words you can edit and riff from.

Let’s roll up our sleeves and see how AI can write for us. For fiction writing, we let AI work scene by scene. Remember that AI’s response is based on the words inside an LLM’s context window. Chapter content, particularly those with alternate points of view or different settings, can confuse the AI by introducing unrelated or contradictory details into its context window. It can cause elements of one scene to bleed into another scene. We will discuss this in more detail when we present the techniques of context stuffing and megaprompting.

Here is a breakdown of how AI can help you with your first draft.

Busting Writers Block: have you ever tried freewriting to overcome writer’s block? You know, the exercise where you sit down and write gibberish or anything that comes to mind about your characters and what they’re supposed to be doing in a particular scene? Freewriting helps get your creative juices flowing as it immerses you into your character’s world and the problems facing him. Well, AI can definitely help here. You can chat with AI about your scene and bounce ideas on how to start or ask AI to write the scene by copying and pasting the information you gathered in the planning step. You’ll notice that the “quality” depends on how much or little information you feed the AI. However, if all you care about is jumpstarting your writing, having AI attempt a starting point is often enough to get you going.

Filling in the Blanks: Another way you can use AI in the drafting process is to ask AI to suggest words, descriptions, dialogue snippets, and transitions. Let’s say you’re writing a scene, and you’d like to add some local color to your setting. You can ask AI to make up a bakery and describe it. You can also ask it to introduce walk-on characters and a funny situation or to make up a town legend on the fly. Perhaps you aren’t good at writing fight scenes. You can prompt the beginning of the fight scene and then ask AI to add in blows, kicks, and punches or describe the sword and armor and how the sequence should go. The possibilities are endless. Your AI assistant is always on hand to give you suggestions or fill in details.

Enhancing prose: Another way AI can help you is by rewriting sections of prose. Let’s say your character talks like a Valley Girl. You can write her dialogue in plain vanilla, copy and paste it into an LLM, and ask it to rewrite it using Valley Girl slang. I don’t know if this is an “enhancement” or not, but it’s certainly a feature. Again, you can explore different styles and voices. You might find that AI rewriting your prose deletes your voice, and it’s not something you care for. That’s okay, too, as you can always edit or rewrite whatever it gives you. The current LLMs tend to “overwrite” with too many adjectives and adverbs. The solution is obvious. Get AI to write or rewrite, see if there’s an improvement, and then edit the prose to your liking. Or you can try another LLM and see if you like its prose better. As you can see, working with AI is truly a collaboration and not a one-way street.

Freeform Writing: A simple way of getting AI to write portions of a scene is to begin the scene on your own. Then feed your partial scene into the LLM and ask for it to either “continue writing” or “continue with these plot points and beats that you specify.” This is a technique called completion prompting. Results vary based on what you put in, but it is an easy way to get past a block. You either like what it gives you or dislike it, and that sparks ideas for you to continue. If you’re a pantser or discovery writer like me, this might be the only technique you use as you tandem write through your story. AI can allow you to brainstorm at every step or story beat. Or explore several paths if you can’t decide. You can even prompt the AI to write an outline (or several outlines) for the rest of the book based on the options available after each scene. This is rapid prototyping and might save backtracking or throwing out many chapters of exploration if you were to write out every scene in detail.

Drafting an entire scene: Having AI write scene prose is the holy grail for some writers and anathema for others. Suffice it to say that an LLM will not write anything other than a generic scene if you give it a one-line prompt. Remember all our work in the last section with story information, character details, settings, and plot points? Effective scene writing requires a lot of prompt engineering and sequencing, as well as providing data to ensure narrative continuity. The current AI assistants work best when given data in small, manageable chunks. Hence, the best practices involve giving it a scene brief or plan containing background information and scene beats. For more details on scene writing, see Part V: Writing Scenes with AI.

TOOLS AND TECHNIQUES FOR WRITING SCENES

Filling in the Blanks and Enhancing Prose: Use chatbots by copying and pasting a partial scene with instructions on what you want to be filled in. Use a tool like Sudowrite or Novelcrafter, where you place your cursor or highlight the text you want to be altered and type in instructions or prompts on what you want. These techniques are pretty intuitive, and you will soon develop your own favorite prompts or ways of doing things.

Freeform Writing: Copy and paste a partial scene into a chatbot and ask it to continue. If you want to give more context, pre-seed the chatbot with background information. This technique is called megaprompting or context stuffing. You are essentially giving the LLM enough context to shift its responses to be relevant to your scene. We’ll talk about context windows in the Advanced LLM Concepts chapter, but these days, the models are growing in context window size, so you have less to worry about than a year ago when we had to count “tokens” like pinching pennies. Using a custom GPT that fits your genre will help the LLM adhere to genre guidelines. For example, if you’re writing a romance, a romance writing Custom GPT is more likely to include romantic tension and banter in the scene than a generic GPT.

Autocrit has recently added an “Inspiration Studio” feature. With this feature, you can place your cursor anywhere in your document and ask, “What Happens Next?” It’ll answer in several categories: Heighten Tension, Reveal Character Motivation, Unexpected Twist, Most Likely, and Outlandish.

Drafting an entire scene: Preparing scene briefs or plans helps guide the AI in writing your scene. Remember that you are the author of the scene briefs or plans, and the more detail you put into it, the better the result. Please see Chapter 31: Using Scene Briefs for more information. You can also fine-tune models to create a unique narrative voice. See Part VI: Personalizing AI for Your Creative Vision.

Because scene writing requires more data and moving parts, using a tool such as Sudowrite, Novelcrafter, or Future Fiction Academy Rexy is preferable to copying and pasting large chunks of data into a chatbot window. It is doable, but in my experience, the chatbots are limited in the number of words they return. Furthermore, you cannot “tune” the parameters of an LLM, and it is hard to try different LLMs as you have to go to different windows (unless you are using an aggregator like Openrouter.ai). Future Fiction Academy’s Rexy Wordbanger is the power tool that allows you to sequence prompts and change the LLMs on the fly. It will enable you to generate the same scene multiple times using different LLMs to compare and contrast the results. Watch their YouTube channel for their live writing sessions. (https://www.youtube.com/@FutureFictionAcademy) ⁠1

As you can see, AI’s role in scene writing is exciting and transformative. The AI also requires a lot of hand-holding, and that’s okay because, after all, you are the owner of the story, and it is just the assistant. You can tune and tweak or completely rewrite what it gives you. Writing with AI is a collaborative process, but at the end of the day, you are the author, and therefore, it is up to you to revise, enhance, or use the AI words as inspiration or trash it. The LLM will not have its feelings hurt, and you will benefit from gaining any insights or surprise “hallucinations,” which is the serendipitous and entertaining part of writing with AI. What did it just come up with?

​[ ​9​ ]​

CRITIQUE AND DEVELOPMENT EDITING

Way back, when I was working on my first novel, I joined Critiquecircle.com ⁠1, an online critique group with a point system to ensure reciprocity. I enjoyed the community and learned a lot, but the quality and thoroughness of the critiques were scattershot. Some users focused only on grammar, whereas others gave personal opinions. I used the critiques as best as possible to get a sense of my story but hired a developmental editor to go through my novel before publishing.

USING AI TOOLS FOR CRITIQUE AND STORY ANALYSIS

1. Story Structure

Plot and Structure Analysis: identify the exposition, rising action, climax, falling action, and resolution, and assess how effectively they are structured to create a compelling narrative.

Pacing Evaluation: analyze the story’s pace and identify sections that may be too slow, too fast, or unevenly paced.

Plot Holes and Inconsistencies: Track information across long stretches of text, which allows it to spot plot holes, inconsistencies, and unresolved plot lines.

2. Character Development

Character Arcs and Motivations: track the development of characters throughout the story, analyzing their motivations, goals, and internal conflicts.

Character Relationships: assess how characters interact with each other, the dynamics of their relationships, and how these relationships influence the plot.

Characterization Techniques: analyze how the author uses dialogue, actions, thoughts, and descriptions to reveal characters’ personalities and inner lives.

3. Theme and Meaning

Identifying Themes: identify the main themes explored in the novel, including love, loss, redemption, justice, and the human condition.

Symbolism and Motifs: Recognize recurring symbols and motifs and analyze how they contribute to the story’s thematic development.

Author’s Message: By analyzing themes and symbols, the AI can infer the author’s message or the underlying meaning they intend to convey.

4. Setting and Atmosphere

World-Building: assess the effectiveness of the author’s world-building, including creating believable settings, cultures, and societies.

Atmosphere and Mood: analyze how the author uses sensory details and language to create a specific atmosphere or mood that enhances the story.

5. Point of View and Narration

Narrative Voice and Perspective: identify the narrative voice and point of view used in the story, such as first-person, third-person limited, or omniscient.

Reliability of the Narrator: assess the narrator’s reliability and analyze how their perspective influences the reader’s understanding of events.

6. Language and Style

Sentence Structure and Word Choice: analyze the author’s use of language, including sentence structure, diction, and figurative language.

Tone and Style: Identify the tone and style of the writing and assess how they contribute to the story’s overall effect.

Dialogue Effectiveness: analyze the effectiveness of dialogue in revealing characters’ personalities and advancing the plot.

INTERACTIVE CRITIQUING WITH A CHATBOT

Like we wrote a story scene-by-scene, we can critique each scene with a chatbot such as ChatGPT or Claude. We can start a running conversation by copying and pasting each scene into the chat and asking for a general critique or specific points we are concerned about.

OpenAI’s ChatGPT Plus allows users to create Custom GPTs with custom knowledge base files. I’ve used this feature to create a Custom GPT called “Writer’s Room.” I gave names to each writer in the writer’s room and his or her field of expertise. One is a dialogue expert who looks for effective dialogue and subtext and advises on how to make dialogue clear and effective. Another could be an expert in character analysis, and someone else could be a world-builder. (You can also use Custom Instructions to Creates “Writer’s Room w/ OpenAI ChatGPT 4” https://adorable-porcupine.super.site/openai-chatgpt I believe Custom Instructions is now available with the Free version) ⁠2

Take the categories I listed in the previous section and create a persona skilled at analyzing that attribute. Upload specific knowledge base files using your preferred story structure, character traits, world-building details, and genre conventions. If you have websites with more knowledge, you can retrieve that data through API calls. Be careful not to overload the knowledge base because your chat response time will be slower while it spins while going through the knowledge base.

You don’t have to use a Custom GPT. The foundational models have enough knowledge of fiction to provide critiques. I’ve heard of authors using Claude 3 Haiku for critiques and editing. Of course, there will always be a flavor of the week, so joining an author’s group will help you keep up.

Here are some ways to use your Writer’s Room or generic chatbot.

1. You could ask the LLM to analyze a specific section of your text and provide feedback on the pacing and tension. For example, “Analyze the pacing and tension in the following excerpt and suggest how it might be improved to increase engagement.”

2. Ask the LLM specific questions about the text, such as “Does the action in this section feel rushed?” or “Is there enough tension in this dialogue to keep readers interested?”

3. Provide the LLM with different scene versions and ask which one maintains better tension or pacing and why. Be sure to tag the scene with container tags so the LLM knows which one is Scene A and which one is Scene B. [Scene A]{paste in Scene A text}[/Scene A].

4. Ask the LLM to describe a chapter’s or scene’s emotional arc and suggest modifications to enhance the emotional impact or smooth out narrative inconsistencies.

PRE-PACKAGED FICTION CRITIQUE TOOLS

You can also use pre-packaged tools like Autocrit, Fictionary, and ProwritingAid.

Autocrit has a new Story Analyzer feature that uses Generative-AI to analyze the following:

Synopsis

Conflict

Characters

World Building

Possible Contradiction Events

Timeline Analysis

Foreshadowing Events

Plot Thread Tracking

Genre Analysis

It works on one chapter at a time.

ProwritingAid uses AI to analyze 4000 words at a time to give feedback on the following:

Strengths

Plot/Story

Characters

Tension

Point of View

Setting

Style/Voice

Clarity

Etc.

Fictionary has an existing story analysis tool that compares your story to a predefined structure. They are currently adding generative AI. For example, the conflict and tension section is analyzed by AI. As of this writing, most of the rest is done conventionally, with user input where needed to keep track of the story threads. However, the platform is evolving, so by the time you read this, many more areas will be AI-enabled.

The same goes for just about every tool you use. Generative AI is embedded everywhere, and you will see it in your writing tools, browsers, and apps.

THE ADVANTAGES OF INTERACTING DIRECTLY WITH LANGUAGE MODELS

While using prepackaged software is convenient and easy, you are limited to the features they’ve provided, and moreover, you cannot access the prompts they send. Therefore, you cannot modify the results by refining the prompts or personalizing them to your specific genre or story. You cannot choose the LLM to ask questions and are limited to the ones they support. The responses you get are likely to be generic because the prompts are generic.

Most of the foundational models from large corporations have filters that prevent them from responding to content they deem violent or sexual; however, open-source LLMs exist that are unfiltered. The responses you get are likely to be generic.

My personal opinion is to go directly to the LLM. That way, you know their data handling policy, whether your data will be used for training, and the size or context window being analyzed. You will also have clarity on the exact prompts passed to the LLM and can ask clarifying follow-up questions to target areas of your manuscript better. Individualized prompts will ensure that your results do not sound like every other user of a particular tool. Going directly to the LLM may mean paying per API call, but if you think about it, you get precisely what you pay for rather than aggregating your monthly charge among all the prepackaged tool’s users. Furthermore, the calls are fractions of pennies. For example, you can see the pricing chart at Openrouter.ai, which includes many FREE models.

As of this writing, Google’s Gemini 1.5 Pro introduced a million-token context window that allows the entire analysis of documents (and even multiple documents). This presents a quantum leap in synthesizing plot threads across chapters and tracking character arcs across books in a series.

Finally, no AI LLM can give the human touch necessary for a complete developmental edit. This includes emotional experiences, puzzling plot threads, cultural considerations, and plain old common sense. However, the conversation with the LLM can point to areas that need further work.

See Part VII. Your AI-Enabled Second Brain for story critique examples.

​[ ​10​ ]​

POLISHING AND PUBLISHING

Many authors regularly use grammar and spellcheckers to polish their manuscripts before sending them to editors. Today’s generative AI tools can be added to the list. LLMs like ChatGPT and Claude were trained on a vast corpus of human-created writing. They can look for patterns and identify areas that you’re concerned with. Their vast associative abilities mean they can provide insight you might not have thought of. In any case, using LLMs to polish your scenes can’t hurt. They offer an additional layer of consideration that complements your human editor.

TIPS ON USING AI FOR EDITING

Ask the same questions of the AI editor as you would yourself. You can copy and paste your scene into its context window and ask specific questions.

  • Read this scene and give me an analysis that includes (you need first to check what the AI sees in the scene).

  • Look for elements in the scene that don’t move the plot forward.

  • Are the people in the scene moving or acting toward their objectives?

  • Is the dialogue relevant to the character’s objectives?

  • Do the actions move the story forward if you have a sequence, such as a fight scene?

  • Are the characters’ motivations clear?

  • Are there unnecessary repetitions of events?

  • Let me know if there are places to cut anything to clarify the narrative drive.

These are only example questions. One way to increase the accuracy of AI’s suggestions is to upload background information such as genre, sub-genre, your vision for the book or scene in question, where this book fits in the marketplace, target audience, and reading level.

You can do this with context stuffing or using a megaprompt. See Chapter 21: Megaprompting.

AI EDITING PRINCIPLES

Supplement, Don’t Replace: AI tools should be used as supplements to human judgment, not replacements. It’s crucial to review AI suggestions critically and retain the final say in all edits to preserve the author’s unique voice.

Explore Different Tools: Different AI editing tools have unique strengths. Experiment with various options to find the ones that best suit your specific needs.

Incorporate Human Feedback: Even the most advanced AI cannot fully replace the nuanced understanding of a human editor or beta reader. Ensure your manuscript undergoes human review to capture subtleties that AI might miss.

USING CONVENTIONAL EDITING TOOLS

AI-powered editing tools like Grammarly, ProWritingAid, and AutoCrit leverage advanced algorithms to analyze text for grammar, style, and clarity issues. A few of their main features, in addition to their generative AI suggestions, are:

  • Catching Typos and Grammatical Errors

  • Improving Sentence Structure and Clarity

  • Enhancing Vocabulary and Style

Another way to proofread your work is to use text-to-audio tools. Having someone or something read back your manuscript is a highly effective way for authors to catch errors that might be missed when reading text visually. Hearing your words can also provide a new perspective on the rhythm and flow of your writing, highlighting areas that may need further refinement.

MARKETING AND PROMOTIONAL MATERIALS

Marketing is beyond the scope of this book, but I’ll mention a few obvious uses of generative AI.

Artwork and Blurbs: AI-driven design tools like Canva ⁠1 or tools powered by DALL-E or Adobe Firefly can generate book covers and marketing graphics. AI can also help craft compelling blurbs by analyzing successful books in your genre to determine what appeals to readers.

Social Media and Blog Content: AI tools can generate social media posts, blog articles, and even podcast transcripts that maintain a consistent promotional voice for your book.

Audiobooks and Video Clips: AI voice synthesis technologies can transform your manuscript into an audiobook. Similarly, AI video creation platforms enable authors to produce book trailers and promotional video clips that can enhance online visibility.

Comprehensive Marketing Analysis: AI tools can be used to research market trends and reader preferences, analyze competitors, and determine what the target audience wants.

The prompting techniques you hone during the story conception and development phase will also help you clarify your marketing goals and generate engaging content geared toward your target audience. AI technology will be ubiquitous in every aspect of your life, and learning to harness it will prove valuable for your success in the competitive literary and publishing marketplace.

​[ ​11​ ]​

ADDITIONAL CONSIDERATIONS

Using AI is an individual choice and should be respected as long as it is used ethically. Let’s discuss several top-of-mind issues.

1. Using generative AI is unethical because it is trained on people’s copyrighted work.

The ethics of using generative AI are complex, as different language models are trained on various datasets. While some LLMs may have been trained on datasets that included copyrighted material scraped from the internet, others are trained exclusively on licensed data. Therefore, it’s unfair to paint all AI with a broad brush. While it is true that some datasets might have included copyrighted material, the case law isn’t settled. Previous cases have found that machine learning is covered under fair use, similar to when you check out a book from the library and read it cover to cover. You learned from the book, but you don’t have a carbon copy of the book in your memory, and neither does the LLM. I’m not a lawyer, so we’ll see how the cases settle. As an AI user, you can mitigate potential ethical concerns by choosing LLMs trained on licensed data.

2. Generative AI enables plagiarism by making it easy for people to plagiarize.

AI language models are powerful tools, but the user is ultimately responsible for their use. If you enter a prompt asking the AI to recreate specific content or copy and paste someone else’s work into the prompt, you are the one committing a potential copyright violation, not the AI. The language model associates words based on the input you provide, so any instances of plagiarism or infringement result from the user’s actions.

We should note, however, that occasionally, even without deliberate infringement, AI-generated content might produce unintentional similarities with existing works due to the vast amount of data used in training. The legal doctrines of fair use and transformative works are still being interpreted and applied to AI-generated content.

Users should also be aware that their prompts may be recorded and stored, potentially serving as evidence in future legal cases unless they use a private, offline language model. Therefore, it is crucial to use AI responsibly and ethically and understand the potential consequences of your actions.

3. Using AI could perpetuate potential biases in the AI models.

This is true because the biases were in the datasets. These datasets contain all known human-recorded text, art, photographs, videos, and audio throughout history. The LLM was trained on these datasets and will reflect those biases. However, this is where the AI users should provide oversight and take responsibility for the output. This is the same if you researched in a library and found biases.

Some ways to mitigate the impact of biases are to fact-check information and seek feedback from diverse perspectives. Any content you produce with AI assistance needs to be critically evaluated. When necessary, you can manually edit the output to correct any mistakes.

4. You cannot copyright AI-generated work.

This varies from country to country. AI-generated writing is already copyrightable in some countries, whereas other countries have determined that you may copyright arrangement of public domain content. The issue is not settled, but generative AI is inside every creative tool or making its way into every tool, and it will be a can of worms to determine the “originality” of a particular work. Some countries consider AI-generated work in the public domain; however, the arrangement or modifications can be copyrighted (with arguments on how much was changed).

I won’t list any specific country and definition of what is copyrightable and what is not because things are changing fast. However, we can look at the case of photography for clues on how the copyright issue might be settled.

In many jurisdictions, the copyright for a photograph is granted to the person who captured the image, regardless of the level of creativity or originality involved in the process. This protection is based on factors such as the choice of camera angle, timing, and the decision to take the photograph. Similarly, the human input involved in creating AI-generated work, such as designing prompts, refining outputs, and selecting the final result, could potentially be considered a basis for granting copyright protection.

However, it is essential to recognize that the legal landscape surrounding AI-generated work is still evolving, and current information may quickly become outdated. Therefore, staying informed about the latest developments in copyright law for your jurisdiction is essential. Organizations such as the World Intellectual Property Organization (WIPO) and national copyright offices can provide up-to-date information and resources on the legal status of AI-generated work.

The increasing integration of AI in creative tools and the rapid advancement of AI technologies will likely lead to further discussions and potential changes in copyright law. Key areas of focus may include the role of human input in the creative process, the concept of originality in the context of AI-generated work, and the balance between protecting creators’ rights and fostering innovation in the AI space.

5. How will AI affect the publishing industry?

Do you have a crystal ball? My answer is that it will definitely affect the publishing industry just like it will affect all aspects of our lives. However, I don’t know the immediate or long-term effects. We live in exciting times.

6. Can I build a career as an AI-assisted author?

You sure can. AI can help your productivity, but the stories you tell still come from your human individuality. Whether you’re an established or emerging author, your success will depend on your storytelling skills, marketing efforts, and ability to connect with readers.

7. AI-generated stories are bland and generic.

This is where prompting makes a difference. If you use generic prompts, you will get generic stories. I’m not a big proponent of collecting other people’s prompts. Writing unique prompts is the art of putting your soul into the story. In addition, filtering, selecting, and revising or using the AI-generated content as inspiration or even “what not to do” goes a long way toward making your story uniquely yours.

Early ChatGPT responses tend to be more clichéd and same-sounding. However, that was due to the dataset where they scraped the internet and fan fiction sites. Now that we have a proliferation of LLMs trained on diverse datasets, we can expect a broader range of results. Furthermore, the content you put in your prompts will influence generative AI’s output. The more imagination you put in, the more likely AI will give you back unique content.

As for AI writing sounding the same, that is no longer true. Most people’s notion of how AI sounds is based on ChatGPT’s default writing style. We can now fine-tune GPT-3.5 to take on an author’s voice. Therefore, in the final analysis, it is not AI making the story bland and generic, but the user copying other people’s prompt libraries and sounding like everyone else using the same prompts.

Stories should be judged on how well the author’s soul touched your soul, whether AI was used or not.

​[ ​12​ ]​

RESOURCES AND REFERENCES

Even though AI can expand our horizons and appears to have vast knowledge, you, as the storyteller, must bring your domain expertise, story-crafting skills, and individuality into the story development process. AI can draw on a vast amount of word associations, but it needs you to direct it and filter the results.

As the author, you are the final arbiter of what you use and how you adapt AI to your writing process. We talked about creating templates for story structure or character development as well as genre-specific scene beats and themes.

There are many resources for learning the craft of writing, so I’ll leave you with a few here. The Story Grid scene development method is useful for scene briefs and John Truby’s books for story structure and genre-specific expectations. To preserve the individuality of your stories, I don’t recommend copying anyone’s story structure or beat outline. However, knowing the craft and how stories and scenes progress, you can create templates tailored to your own work.

​[ ​PART 3​ ]​

ADVANCED PROMPTING

​[ ​13​ ]​

PROMPT DESIGN

What is a prompt?

It is the request or message you send to the AI or LLM to get a response. A prompt is formed with natural language rather than coding language. To talk to an LLM or AI model, you frame a request or a question and type it or speak it into the model’s input box.

Since the LLM is a context-based word association tool, your prompt seeds its context window with words to associate, directing it to put together a response.

As you interact with an LLM, you might discover that the answers you’re getting are not what you wanted. Perhaps the LLM didn’t give you enough information, or it misunderstood your prompt and went in a different direction. This is where prompt engineering or prompt design comes in.

By carefully constructing prompts, you can get the LLM to return more relevant or satisfying results. We’re giving the LLM relevant context to steer it in the direction you want it to go. Remember, the GPT is a word association machine, and words can mean different things in different contexts.

The prompt is your opportunity to include the words and phrases that matter to your story. It is a compelling way to differentiate your results from those of someone else. I don’t go with those “prompt encyclopedias” that people are selling or “secret prompts” playbooks. It’s better to understand the principles of prompting and then create prompts that are individualized for your particular story or task.

One thing to note: Prompt design does not alter the pre-trained parameters in the model. It simply alters the distribution of the likely words to be returned. It is easy to do and experiment with. Small changes in the prompt could affect significant changes in the results, which is a big positive for creative writing or any other application.

​[ ​14​ ]​

ELEMENTS OF A BASIC PROMPT

The most basic prompting technique is to provide clear and detailed instructions to the LLM so that it can effectively return a response that meets your needs.

WHO, WHAT, HOW

Let’s first consider the following questions.

Who: Who are you, and what are you looking for? This provides the context to the LLM in terms of the consumer of the result.

What: What are you asking or wanting the LLM to do? This provides the specific instruction and any input (or background) data you want the LLM to work on.

How: This indicates the type of output or response you expect from the LLM.

The objective is to communicate your goals clearly to the LLM so that you receive an accurate and relevant output.

Here is an example.

<Prompt>

I am a developmental editor who drafts emails for my romance writing clients. Please suggest several eye-catching email titles that will enhance my open rate. This is the email I’m sending [copy and paste the email into the prompt]. I want the style to be punchy and upbeat.

</Prompt>

This prompt is more specific than the first prompt you likely would have entered:

<Prompt>

Please give me a good title for this email [copy and paste the email into the prompt].

</Prompt>

Another way of prompting is to add an audience and their needs with a motivational goal you want to obtain. This gives you more input on what you want and suggests the “how” to appeal to that audience and their needs.

<Prompt>

I am a marketing consultant conducting a workshop on how to use social media to generate organic leads for small business owners interested in expanding their customer base and enhancing their brand visibility online. Write an engaging email to motivate the client to attend my workshop [copy and paste workshop agenda]. Use a friendly tone of voice.

</Prompt>

TEMPLATE-BASED PROMPTING

Additional information could be included as a template. The LLM “gets” that a colon suggests information for it to fill in.

Here is an example of giving the AI a “template” to fill out.

<Prompt>

I am writing a compelling and engaging product description for a book that readers can’t put down. Please write me a bestselling product description blurb for a contemporary romance with the following elements.

The hook between the protagonists:

Initial attraction and conflict:

Intriguing elements that pique romance reader interest:

Main crisis point and conflict dynamics:

What’s at risk:

Here is the story summary for you to analyze {copy and paste in story summary}. Please limit the output to less than 1000 words.

</Prompt>

The key to remember is that any LLM, just like an intern or assistant, will give you better results when you lay out specific details and expectations. Fortunately, prompting can be iterative, and you can improve on the results by telling the LLM what you liked and didn’t like. But the Who, What, How technique sets the stage for effective prompting.

POSITIVE PROMPTING

By telling the AI what you’re looking for and how you want the results, you are aiding its ability to construct the answers that may prove more useful to you. Positive feedback gives you better results because the LLM is a word-association engine. For example, if you tell it what you don’t like, those words end up in its context window.

We’ve all had the experience of telling a child, “Don’t touch the cookies or leave your socks on the floor or eat before washing your hands,” only to find out that the child did everything you told it not to do. This is because the tiny word “don’t” did not register as much as the rest of your commands. The same is true with AI, where you’re essentially stuffing its context window with everything you don’t want it to do.

For example, saying “show, don’t tell, and don’t use flowery language and too many adverbs and dialogue tags” doesn’t work as well as stating your commands in positive terms. Instead of “show, don’t tell,” try saying, “Describe the progression of the scene in detailed action and dialogue.” Similarly, “don’t use flowery language” does not work as well as “write with a direct tone using simplistic language.”

REMINDER PROMPTS

As the conversation progresses, the LLM may “forget” things you discussed earlier. This happens because the earlier words have fallen outside the context window, or “memory.” You will have to refresh the information you give it by reminding it or regularly summarizing the results of your discussion to keep that information fresh.

As you can see, improved prompt design or engineering can do a lot. Skillful prompting saves editing time since you get results that are more suited to your needs.

​[ ​15​ ]​

ROLE-BASED PROMPTS

Role-playing is a method that can get an actor into character. As a fiction author, you might have used role-playing or personas to either interview your characters or get into your character’s head. This method also works with an LLM. For example, if you want the AI to act as a therapist, you’d like to push it in the direction of therapy terminology and associations. This makes the AI access those word sequences better aligned with your goals.

By assigning a specific role or persona to the AI, you provide a clear framework for its responses. Role-based prompts are also flexible. You can refine the role as you go by nudging it in the direction it gives you based on its responses.

Want to brainstorm ideas for a gritty dystopian thriller? Assign your AI the role of a seasoned post-apocalyptic fiction editor with a knack for dark, twisted plots. Need help fleshing out the intricate magic system for your epic fantasy series? Cast your AI as a veteran fantasy world-builder with a deep understanding of the genre’s tropes and traditions.

You’re essentially seeding the AI’s context window with words relevant to the desired results. You’ll also be surprised how agile today’s advanced LLMs can adapt to a role.

THE ADVANTAGES OF ROLE-BASED INSTRUCTIONS

Compared to plain vanilla prompts, which state a request or ask a question, role-based prompts offer several key advantages:

Clarity and Focus: A role allows the LLM to focus on the results you want. It also adds to the specificity of good prompting. For instance, instead of asking, “Write a scene about a conflict,” you can instruct the AI to “Act as a screenwriter and write a tense scene where the protagonist confronts the antagonist, building towards a dramatic climax.”

Expertise and Authority: Role-based prompts allow you to leverage the AI’s knowledge and capabilities within specific domains. By assigning roles such as “expert historian,” “experienced detective,” or “renowned scientist,” you tap into the AI’s vast universe of training data and guide it to provide responses that reflect that expertise.

Perspective and Voice: Role-playing prompts enable you to explore different perspectives and voices within your story. You can instruct the AI to act as a specific character, a narrator with a particular tone, or even an inanimate object, gaining valuable insights and enriching your narrative with diverse viewpoints. You can also add details about the role. Instead of asking your AI to “act as a romance novelist,” try something like: “You are a bestselling romance author with a penchant for witty banter and slow-burn relationships. You have a knack for crafting swoon-worthy heroes and relatable heroines. Provide feedback on my character dynamics and suggest ways to build romantic tension.”

Consistency and Coherence: Assigning a consistent role to the AI throughout your project helps maintain coherence in its responses and ensures its outputs align with the overall tone and style of your story. You can do this in each thread of a chat, but be sure to repeat the role-based prompt every so often. If you have ChatGPT 4, you can place your role-based prompt in the Custom Instructions. However, don’t forget to turn it off if you start another conversation for another project. It is a bit of a pain, so I just put it in the chat every so often, and this allows me to refine the role as the chat proceeds.

Creative Exploration: Role-based prompts can spark new ideas and push the boundaries of your creativity. By challenging the AI to think outside the box and adopt different personas, you may discover unexpected narrative twists, character motivations, or world-building elements.

EXAMPLES OF ROLE-BASED PROMPTS IN ACTION

World-Building: “Act as a medieval cartographer and describe the layout of a bustling port city, including its key landmarks, trade routes, and defensive fortifications.”

Character Development: “Imagine you are a renowned psychologist. Analyze the protagonist’s motivations and inner conflicts, considering their past experiences and current challenges.”

Plot Development: “Take on the role of a seasoned mystery writer and suggest three possible suspects for the crime, each with a compelling motive and alibi.”

Scene Writing: “Become a film director and write a scene where the protagonist escapes from a high-security prison, focusing on suspenseful pacing and vivid descriptions of the environment.”

WHY GENRE FICTION AUTHORS SHOULD EMBRACE ROLE-BASED PROMPTS

Genre fiction, with its established conventions and reader expectations, presents unique opportunities for leveraging role-based prompts. Here’s why:

Genre-Specific Expertise: By assigning roles that align with your chosen genre, you can tap into the AI’s knowledge of genre tropes, character archetypes, and common plot structures.

World-Building Authenticity: Role-based prompts can help create immersive and believable worlds by drawing on the AI’s understanding of historical settings, futuristic technologies, or fantastical elements.

Character Archetypes and Development: Guide the AI to explore different character archetypes within your genre, ensuring your cast resonates with readers’ expectations while also offering fresh and engaging personalities.

Plot Twists and Suspense: Utilize role-playing to explore alternative plot lines, generate suspenseful scenarios, and surprise readers with unexpected twists that adhere to genre conventions.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTIONS

Most chatbots do not have system instructions, but I want to mention it here because they are instructions used by some LLMs as an overriding “global” instruction to the LLM about the role they are playing, tone or style of the output, or any additional rules or guidance. See Chapter 25 for more on System Prompts.

If you are using an interface, such as Google AI Studio, that allows you to put in a System Instruction or System Message, then placing the role into that box means you don’t have to keep repeating it for every prompt.

Otherwise, you will need to remind the LLM every so often what role it is playing.

​[ ​16​ ]​

ITERATIVE PROMPTING

As writers, we’re masters of using dialogue to elicit information. That is why iterative prompting is natural for us. At its core, iterative prompting is a conversation—a back-and-forth exchange between you, the author, and your AI writing partner.

You provide a prompt and then evaluate the responses. You then give feedback to the AI and refine subsequent prompts. It’s an intuitive process that mirrors the process of writing and editing. This iterative process allows authors to collaborate with the AI, gradually shaping the generated content to align with their creative vision and achieve the desired results.

All by asking clarifying questions.

ADVANTAGES OF ITERATIVE PROMPTING

Gradual Learning Curve: Iterative prompting allows authors to start with simple prompts and gradually increase complexity as they become more comfortable with the AI and its capabilities.

Flexibility and Control: The iterative approach empowers authors to maintain control over the AI’s output and steer the direction of the generated content, which can be reassuring for those new to using AI.

Refining Ideas and Concepts: Through iteration, authors can gradually refine their story ideas, character development, and world-building elements, exploring different possibilities and discovering new directions with AI’s assistance.

Improving Accuracy and Relevance: By evaluating the AI’s responses and adjusting prompts accordingly, authors can ensure the generated content is accurate, relevant to the story, and consistent with the established narrative.

Training the AI within its Context Window: By giving the LLM feedback, iterative prompts allow the user to influence the AI’s results within its context window. Of course, this “training” is not permanent because the GPTs are “pre-trained.” However, by refining your prompts, you are showing the LLM what you currently desire.

STEPS IN THE ITERATIVE PROMPTING PROCESS

Initial Prompt: Start with a clear and concise prompt that conveys your basic idea or request.

Evaluation: Analyze the AI’s response, considering its strengths, weaknesses, and alignment with your vision.

Refinement: Based on your evaluation, refine your next prompt to provide additional guidance, clarify expectations, or redirect the AI’s focus.

Iteration: Repeat steps 2 and 3, continuing the cycle of evaluation and refinement until you achieve the desired results.

EXAMPLES OF ITERATIVE PROMPTING

Initial Prompt: “Describe a strong and independent female character.”

AI Response: [redacted]

Follow-up Prompt: “With this description, please layer three short-term goals that Anya has and her motivations for those goals.”

AI Response: [redacted]

Followup Prompt: “Looking at her goals and motivations, what sorts of conflicts will stymie her, and how will she react?”

AI Response: [redacted]

Follow-up Prompt: “These are great; however, you’ve only shown positive reactions to these conflicts. To create a well-rounded and interesting character, Anya will need some flaws or areas of emotional growth. Please rephrase her approaches to these conflicts in a way that highlights a flaw in her character and how each conflict can help her overcome the flaw and turn a weakness into a strength.”

AI Response: [redacted]

Now we’re getting somewhere. We don’t have a “perfect protagonist” who excels in every endeavor.

Follow-up Prompt: “Great. Now that you know Anya’s strengths, weaknesses, and emotional tenor, please design a love interest who can bring out both the best and worst in her.”

As you can see, iterative prompting is intuitive and natural for a writer, and I suspect you already do this naturally. Combining it with specificity, details, and role-playing will help you get results shaped to your creative vision.

Tips for Effective Iterative Prompting

It’s important to approach it with intention and strategy to get the most out of iterative prompting. Here are some best practices to keep in mind:

1. Start with a clear goal: Use the best practices we discussed before, with who, what, how, and role-playing to give the AI the best context. Are you looking to flesh out a character’s backstory? Brainstorm plot twists? Enrich your story’s setting. A specific focus will help guide your prompts and keep the iterative process on track.

2. Be specific in your feedback and follow-up prompts: When evaluating the AI’s responses, provide clear and constructive feedback. Highlight what you like and what you don’t, and be specific about what you’d like to see more or less of in future iterations. The more guidance you can give, the better the AI can learn and adapt to your preferences.

3. Embrace experimentation: Don’t be afraid to try different approaches and techniques. Prompt the AI to explore your story from different angles or perspectives. Ask it to emulate different writing styles or genres. The beauty of iterative prompting is that you can continually refine and course-correct as needed.

4. Trust the process: Iterative prompting is a journey, not a destination. It takes time and patience to sculpt your story into its final form. Embrace the messiness and uncertainty of the process, and trust that each iteration brings you one step closer to the story you want to tell.

Iterative prompting is a powerful technique for collaborating with AI and shaping its outputs to align with your creative vision. By embracing this dynamic and interactive approach, you can unlock the full potential of AI as a writing partner and elevate your storytelling to new heights.

​[ ​17​ ]​

PROMPT CHAINING

Have you ever told your child to clean their room only to find that the results weren’t what you expected? That is because you gave the child a complex task with many moving parts and did not break it down to what “clean your room” meant or looked like.

Managers often experience the same “lack of results” from their workers when they assign a complex task to an intern or new employee, and the same thing happens with enthusiastic AI assistants when asked to do a task. The management technique that involves breaking down a complex task into smaller, step-by-step tasks is called Work Breakdown Structure (WBS).

We can do the same process by prompt chaining, where a complex prompt is broken down into a series of interconnected prompts to guide the AI model through a logical thought process and achieve more comprehensive and accurate results.

Prompt chaining is like a step-by-step recipe. It gives instructions to the AI in smaller and more specific steps. For example, prompt chains help LLMs think through a mathematical word problem. This is also how children are taught to approach word problems without “skipping steps.”

Prompt chains in fiction might involve asking the LLM to construct a rough sketch of a setting and then returning to fill in the details. Remember, a prompt chain is a predetermined sequence. It does not vary with the evaluation of the AI’s response.

Breaking down a task into smaller, interconnected tasks is a method for obtaining a richer final result. For example, if you asked AI to describe a cat, it would give you a generic description. Using a logical sequence of steps, you can encourage the AI’s outputs to remain consistent and coherent and go to greater depth and detail.

Elizabeth Ann West taught prompt chaining early on, and many of the ideas in this section come from her methods.

BENEFITS OF PROMPT CHAINING

Exploring Complex Ideas: By breaking down a broad concept into smaller components, you can delve deeper into specific aspects of your story, such as character motivations, world-building details, or plot intricacies.

Generating Creative Solutions: Prompt chains can help the AI model explore multiple possibilities and generate creative solutions to narrative challenges, such as overcoming plot holes or developing unique character arcs.

Maintaining Coherence and Consistency: The step-by-step approach ensures that the AI’s responses remain connected and consistent with the overall story concept, avoiding contradictory or irrelevant outputs.

Identify and Solve Problems in Piece of Prose: Asking the AI to first identify or critique a piece of prose and then fix it or rewrite it gives the LLM clarity on what it is supposed to do at each step.

HOW TO USE PROMPT CHAINING

Identify the Core Concept: Start with the main idea or question you want to explore. Give as much detail as possible using the Who, What, How, and other Prompting techniques.

Break Down the Concept: Divide the core concept into smaller, more manageable steps or sub-questions. These steps should follow a logical sequence and build upon each other.

Create Prompts for Each Step: Formulate individual prompts for each step in the chain, ensuring they are clear, concise, and relevant to the overall concept.

Feed the Prompts Sequentially: Provide the prompts to the AI model one at a time, allowing it to build upon the previous response and develop a chain of thought.

Evaluate and Refine: Analyze the AI’s responses at each step and adjust the subsequent prompts to ensure the chain of thought remains on track and aligns with your goals.

EXAMPLES OF PROMPT CHAINS FOR FICTION WRITING

<prompt chain>

Let’s develop a well-rounded character for a fiction story. Follow these steps:

1. Generate a brief character description, including name, age, occupation, and key personality traits.

2. Provide a detailed backstory for the character, focusing on pivotal moments and experiences that shaped their personality.

3. Describe the character’s primary goal or motivation in the story.

4. Discuss potential conflicts or obstacles the character may face in pursuing their goal.

5. Outline how the character might grow or change throughout the story.

</prompt chain>

<prompt chain>

Help me brainstorm a plot for a mystery novel using the following steps:

1. Generate a crime or mystery that will be the story’s central focus.

2. Introduce the main characters involved in the mystery, including the protagonist, antagonist, and any suspects.

3. Provide a list of potential clues or evidence to help solve the mystery.

4. Describe the primary settings where the story will take place.

5. Outline a series of plot twists or revelations to keep readers engaged throughout the story.

6. Suggest possible resolutions or outcomes for the mystery.

</prompt chain>

<prompt chain>

Let’s create a vivid and immersive fantasy world for a novel. Follow these steps:

1. Describe the general landscape and geography of the world, including any notable landmarks or natural wonders.

2. Outline the different races, creatures, or magical beings that inhabit the world.

3. Explain the world’s system of magic or supernatural powers, including its limitations and consequences.

4. Discuss the political structure and major factions or kingdoms.

5. Provide examples of unique customs, traditions, or cultural practices found in the world.

6. Describe the technology level and key innovations or inventions in the story world.

</prompt chain>

Prompt chains differ from iterative prompting in that the prompt chain is fixed like a recipe, whereas iterative prompting is more like an interrogation, where the user varies the follow-up question based on each situation. Prompt chains work well when we use prompt sequencing to “automate” story generation.

Prompt Chains are an excellent way of developing genre fiction outlines. Each genre has its requirements, obligatory moments, types of characters, and other attributes that a writer needs to fulfill genre convention. Each genre also has required story beats that you can include as a template to guide the LLM. Here is an example of a romance prompt chain.

<prompt chain>

You are a bestselling romance author for small-town romance looking to write {trope} romance involving {specifics, the more detail, the better}

Follow these steps to develop our romance:

1. Give me a hook and a pitch.

2. Suggest a title and an SEO-enhanced subtitle that includes the trope and keywords of interest

3. Name and describe the heroine of this romance. Make her a headstrong and independent woman with a soft heart and a strong sense of justice. Give her strengths and likable traits, as well as an emotional flaw that might stymie her chance for love.

4. Name and describe the hero who will challenge the heroine in every way. Make him attractive and kind-hearted but distrustful due to his family background. Give him strengths and likable traits but an emotional flaw that makes it difficult for him to trust. However, he has a strong sense of justice and concern for the weak.

5. Write a synopsis for this romance that includes a twist that will intrigue and surprise the reader. Adhere to all romance genre conventions.

6. Create a four-act romance structure for this enemies-to-lovers romance with the following romance plot beats in place: A meet-cute or initial connection between would-be lovers:

Attraction and Growing Connection:

Obstacles and Challenges:

Dark Moment, Separation, or Testing Problem:

Reconciliation and Declaration of Love:

Happy Ending:

7. Create a 20-chapter outline for this romance following all romance conventions.

</prompt chain>
