MAINTAINING NARRATIVE CONTINUITY IN REXY WORD BANGER

Rexy Word Banger was designed to be a prompt sequencer out of the box. I will review the big picture of how it’s done; those interested can check out the videos.

1. Place your Story Information, Writing Style, and Scene Brief(s) into your content management system and label them. Remember that the Big Bang Box is analogous to the Assistant Window in Playground. It is the place where the AI puts its response. To get it started, paste your Story So Far into the Big Bang Box (or let Rexy load it from your content management system).

3. Top Prompt: Please read the Story Information, Writing Style, and Story So Far for background on the scene we are going to write.

Bottom Prompt: Please continue the story we are writing with narrative logic consistent with the Story So Far, above. Now, write the scene given in the Scene Brief 1.

4. Read what the AI put in the Big Bang Box. Edit it in place and label it Story So Far.

5. Top Prompt: Please read the Story Information, Writing Style, and Story So Far for background on the scene we are going to write.

Bottom Prompt: Please continue the story we are writing with narrative logic consistent with the Story So Far, above. Now, write the scene given in the Scene Brief 2.

(Continue in this manner as you step through Scene Briefs).

Currently, the content management system is Notion, and the prompts are stored in a Notion database. However, even if this is changed, the notion of prompt sequencing will be preserved and enhanced. The flexibility of Rexy Word Banger means you can chain these prompts together and run them without human intervention if you do not wish to edit what the AI gives you. You can also chain prompts to ask the AI to edit or enhance its output before moving on.

At any stage, you can trim what’s in the Big Bang box to manage the context window, so that if the LLM balks and says it cannot fit more into the context window (you’ll get an error message), you can go back and delete what’s no longer needed, keeping only the most recent material.

It’s best to join the Future Fiction Academy to learn about Rexy. However, if you want a sneak peek, Elizabeth Ann West shows how narrative continuity is maintained in the Big Bang Box in this video, where she writes a short story in 10 minutes in this video: “Nanowrimo in a DAY? I Did 10K Words in 10 Mins!!” (https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=A9lLDiIJ7fw) ⁠3 This video shows how to keep the story consistent by keeping all the scenes inside the Big Bang Box, which is sent every time into the prompt.

​[ ​33​ ]​

TROUBLESHOOTING

Here are some common issues writers encounter when using AI to write scenes. I’ll summarize them below with tips on troubleshooting and improving the process.

Problem:

The AI didn’t generate enough words.

I gave enough material, but it seemed to have petered out or stopped writing.

Consider:

Don’t give the AI a conclusion in the scene plan. It might rush to the conclusion, like problem solved, we’re all holding hands, and together, we’re determined to go forward.

Check your briefs for plot progression and make them more granular.

Check the LLMs context window. Use large context window models and dial up your max-length parameter to 4000 (assuming you are using Rexy Word Banger or one of the Playgrounds that allow parameter tweaking). If you are using the Chat interface, you have no control over the “max-length” parameter. Therefore, you cannot override a short response no matter how you prompt it. The chat interface is a flat-fee service serving many users. If you need finer control, you must go directly to the API or use the Playground or developer interfaces.

Problem:

The AI didn’t follow my scene brief or plan.

Consider:

The temperature might be too high, and the AI might be too creative. Reduce it to .7 or .5.

You might have used too many pronouns. Use character names so that AI knows who is doing what. Sometimes, it might invent new characters if it can’t figure out the actors on the stage.

Your scene brief does not have a logical progression. AI writes based on the context of the previous words. If you switch topics, locations, or the point of view character, it will get confused and continue down the stream of consciousness it was pursuing.

Separate your scene brief into parts and give more detail. Use a new brief for a different point of view or jump to a different location or setting.

Problem:

I don’t like the writing style.

Consider:

This is tricky because the LLMs will interpret the same style instructions differently. Claude 3 Opus, Sonnet, and Haiku are notable examples. They seem to have their own personalities. You can give each of them the same style guide and see how differently they write from it.

Try feeding a piece of writing you want it to emulate through the LLM and ask it to describe the style in a way that a writing assistant can replicate. You might have to use different style guides for different LLMs.

Another thing to consider is fine-tuning an LLM to write in your own style. You do this by feeding your writing into the fine-tuning system. See Part VI: Personalizing AI for Your Creative Vision

Problem:

The AI writing reveals too much or rushes ahead in the scene.

Consider:

Limit the AI’s need to know in the scene brief. Look at the beats from the reader’s point of view as they discover what’s going to happen next. If you want a cliffhanger, don’t tell the AI what it is. Say, end in a cliffhanger and see what it comes up with. You can always lop off anything you don’t want.

Problem:

The LLM didn’t include something that was in its context window.

Consider:

Because the LLM is dealing with hundreds of thousands of tokens, a small piece of information may not be considered significant. Just by random chance, it would have been disregarded in favor of another piece of information. The best way to deal with this is to repeat this critical information near the end of the prompt. This is why we put general story information at the top, followed by previous scenes. The last part of the megaprompt is the current scene brief and the writing instructions, such as point of view, present or past tense, and other information you must have in your scene.

Another way is to re-roll the prompt. Because the LLM is a random word generator, you might get lucky on the next try. You can also use a different LLM or change the Temperature or TopP parameters.

Writing with AI is a collaborative process; you are always free to change things if you don’t like what it gives you. You can either prompt until it gives you what you want or edit or rewrite everything it gave you. You can tweak temperature, TopP, or change models. You can gather all the outputs and pick and choose pieces you like, or you can riff off what they produced and write it in your own words.

There is no wrong way to use AI if you use it ethically with your own prompts, story beats, scene briefs, and fine tunes (where AI personalizes its writing style based on your writing samples). See Part VI: Personalizing AI for Your Creative Voice.

​[ ​34​ ]​

PERSONALIZING AI FOR YOUR CREATIVE VOICE

​[ ​35​ ]​

WHAT IS FINE-TUNING?

One of the most exciting developments for fiction writers is the art of fine-tuning an existing LLM to shape its behavior in a style or format of your choosing. It suggests the possibility of creating a fine tune that writes like you. All you have to do is provide samples of your writing and format your prompts in a way that will elicit the behavior.

In practice, though, it’s not that easy. Finding samples is easy; however, figuring out the prompts to twist and tune the existing LLM to get the result you like is still an art. This is because fine-tuning is not simply stuffing context into an AI’s context window or giving it information to influence its responses.

Fine-tuning changes HOW an LLM behaves; as you’ve seen before, researchers are still surprised by what and how an LLM behaves. Let’s explain in layman’s terminology.

Think of fine-tuning as the process of adding adverbs to an action. Just as adverbs don’t change the action or the information provided, fine-tuning doesn’t add any new information to the model. Instead, it’s about showing the GPT what you want it to do, rather than telling it. For instance, you might start with a plain piece of text and then edit it to match your writing style. By providing it with samples, the aim is to rearrange the GPT’s expression to align with your desired manner.

Other analogies are rearranging the furniture to create a different experience or changing the cooking techniques of a recipe while retaining the same ingredients, for example, beating the eggs rather than folding them. Think of fine-tuning as shaping the personality of the AI and guiding it to express itself in a way that aligns with your own creative vision.

In summary, fine-tuning involves training an existing LLM on a smaller, more specific dataset to adapt its behavior. It trains the GPT in qualitative terms. It doesn’t add any information. It is a style change and exactly what fiction authors look for to get an LLM that “writes like them.”

However, while fine-tuning can improve the AI’s ability to mimic an author’s style, getting there is still a challenge. That’s because we don’t entirely understand how the model will respond, and we have a limited dataset available to try to push the billions or trillions of parameters of its existing training. That said, careful prompting and semantic analysis of your dataset will reap rewards when you have a fine tune that sounds like you.

​[ ​36​ ]​

HOW TO FINE-TUNE

Fine-tuning an LLM to match your writing style requires a curated dataset that reflects your unique voice, tone, and style. The first step is to decide the purpose of your fine tune. If you want to get one to emulate your style, you need to gather writing samples of the tone or style you want the AI to emulate.

FINE-TUNING TIPS

Start by gathering 1000-2000 word samples that reflect your writing style. If your voice is different between, say, romantic suspense and romantic comedy, you might segregate the samples by point of view, tense, or genre.

Include a variety of writing samples, such as dialogue, descriptions, internal monologues, and expository text, to ensure the AI learns the full range of your stylistic expression.

Ensure the writing samples you choose reflect a consistent voice and tone throughout. Perhaps you have a more informal tone for fiction and a formal tone for nonfiction. Consider the purpose of the fine tune, and don’t mix datasets with different goals.

Focus on Recent Work: Include your most recent writing samples, as your style may have evolved.

Respect Copyright: Only use writing samples you have the rights to or are in the public domain. If you have co-authored works, ensure you have permission to use them for fine-tuning.

Select a base model LLM: Currently, OpenAI and Google Gemini allow fine-tuning on their foundational models (that I know of). OpenAI enables fine-tuning of its GPT-3.5 models and previous ones. There is a waiting list for the GPT-4, and Anthropic has announced that it has no interest in fine-tuning its models. They recently released their Claude 3 generation of LLMs in three flavors: Haiku, Sonnet, and Opus. I don’t know how they did it, but these three models have recognizable default writing styles. Perhaps they’ve already been tuned for how malleable they are to stylistic writing prompts.

Meanwhile, the OpenAI LLMs have a voice that many people recognize as “AI-ish” writing. The current model that we can fine-tune is GPT-3.5-16K. In itself, it is not that good of a writer and tends to be very brief and surface-level. I’ve created a fine tune for my romantic comedy style that doesn’t sound like ChatGPT. My fine tune provides snappier dialogue and lighter, more carefree writing. There are internal thoughts and banter minus the usual ChatGPT clichés and the tendency to summarize at the end of a scene. Although it is still GPT-3.5 level writing, I call it a win. Remember what I told you? A fine tune does not add “smarts” or information. It only changes the way the response is presented.

HOW TO FINE TUNE AN OPENAI MODEL

The dataset consists of three portions. Each element is a System, User, or Assistant prompt.

Sounds easy, right? The twist is that you will be providing the Assistant “prompt” as an example of what you want the AI to return, in addition to the System and User prompt that you best believe fits the data you desire.

By doing this, you are showing the LLM what you want from it, in addition to telling it through the System and User Prompt.

Here’s a simple example of a System, User, and Assistant prompt.

System: You are a Snarkifier of Dialogue designed to take ordinary dialogue and make it snarky and sarcastic.

User: Please snarkify this dialogue sample: {copy and paste in boring dialogue line.}

Assistant: {Provide the snarky version of the dialogue}

If these snippets are short, providing 50 to 100 samples is reasonable. However, if we provide 1000-2000 word scenes, you only need to provide 20 samples. You must ensure that your System, User, and Assistant prompts fit into the LLM’s context window. The model they currently recommend is gpt-3.5-turbo-0125.

The dataset must be provided as a JSONL file, which is a major pain unless you use a tool that converts CSV into JSONL. (Rexy has an LLM Tuner that will do this for you). You can then upload the JSONL file to the OpenAI interface, push a button, and let it run.

See OpenAI’s documentation on Fine-Tuning. https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/fine-tuning ⁠1

HOW TO GET A GOOD FINE TUNE OF YOUR WRITING STYLE

Once you have the resulting fine-tuned model, you can try it to see if it meets your needs.

Like everything else, fine-tuning is an iterative process. Follow the instructions to create the fine tune and then evaluate its performance with test prompts. You’ll notice that even if you trained your fine tune with default temperature and topP values at 1.0 and 1.0, it tends to go a little nutty and might spit out gibberish at that temperature level. No one knows why. Perhaps squeezing the model with fine-tuning makes it less predictable. Therefore, I turned the parameters down to 0.7 and 0.7. Some writers go even lower to get the fine-tuned model to follow instructions. (Note, if your fine-tuned model is repetitive, consider lowering the temperature but keeping the TopP higher to increase the diversity of responses).

Here are some tips to increase the usefulness of your fine-tuned model.

Finding the Right Data: Selecting the right training data is crucial for successful fine-tuning. You need enough examples that showcase your writing style and voice while ensuring consistency and quality throughout the dataset.

Prompt Engineering: Crafting effective prompts for fine-tuning is an art in itself. Experiment with different approaches to find what elicits the desired response from the AI and effectively guides its learning process. I’ve found out there are no “shortcuts,” just throwing data at the fine-tuning and hoping it sticks. The user prompt must be specific enough for the task but also general enough to adapt to how you will use the fine-tuned model. This is an area I’m still experimenting with—how regimented or loose can I make the User prompt fit the output while remaining flexible?

Iteration and Refinement: Fine-tuning is an iterative process. It often requires multiple attempts, adjustments to the training data, and experimentation with different parameters to achieve optimal results. There are all sorts of knobs and dials, like a number of epochs, training loss, and an entire “science” to understand. There are also considerations of sample size and overtraining to worry about.

Technical Expertise: If you are interested in writing style, you need to understand how to describe that writing style in a way that the particular LLM you are using describes it. Lexical choices, syntax, and other linguistic attributes matter. One of the Future Fiction Academy authors used a concordance tool (ANTCONC) to understand the frequency and context of his words so that he could have the AI tell him how his voice is described. The concordance tool lets him get a sense of his writing and provides a good description of his writing style.

Epochs and Training Loss: Our datasets are typically an order of magnitude larger than the usual datasets. Our application is creative, so the usual discussion about the number of epochs and training loss doesn’t pertain. The only way to tell if a fine tune works for you is if it works for you. Epochs are the number of times your data is run through the fine-tune training, and training loss should decrease, meaning the fine-tune is getting more “accurate.” However, in fiction, more is not better. Presumably, you can keep training and training until training loss goes to close to zero. However, once it does that, it will converge to an “answer” it believes you want and keep repeating phrases like a parrot. In practice, our training loss is between 1.4 to 2.0, and we run 4 or 5 epochs. If the fine-tuning is too repetitive, it means you’ve overfitted your data, and you should run fewer epochs. However, if your training loss number is too high and you run a few epochs, your fine-tuned model might not differ from the base model.

In the case of fiction, with our creativity and diversity of training data, fine-tuning is truly an art and not a science. As more powerful models allow users to fine-tune them, we may see a day when any author can personalize their AI writing assistant so that the output possesses their unique voice. In addition to tailoring by genre, I can see a day where fine tunes are selected for alternate points of view characters to reflect better how they speak within a novel. A fine tune of 20 samples of 2000 words costs around $3.00, so it doesn’t break the bank. This is with GPT 3.5. Once GPT 4 fine-tuning is generally available, its cost will likely be higher.

Therefore, it doesn’t hurt to give it a try. In the next chapter, I’ll show you how I created two fine tunes and my thinking around them.

​[ ​37​ ]​

MY FINE TUNE EXAMPLES

SIMPLE FIRST-PERSON POV

I did a simplified fine tune using 20 writing samples of 1000-2000 words from my romance novels. I selected scenes from a first-person point of view present tense.

SYSTEM: You are RachAyalaFirstPOVPres, clone of romance author Rachelle Ayala’s writing style in first person present tense point of view. Your job is to write romance novel prose in Rachelle’s style and voice.

USER: Write romance novel prose in Rachelle Ayala’s style in character’s first person present-tense point of view.

ASSISTANT: {1000-2000 words scenes)

Result One:

The result was writing that did not sound like ChatGPT, as the base model is GPT 3.5. It wrote longer scenes than the base model. As a test, I had the fine-tuned model write a simple short story.

Parameters: Temperature=0.7, TopP=0.7

SYSTEM: You are RachAyalaFirstPOVPres, clone of romance author Rachelle Ayala’s writing style in first person present tense point of view. Your job is to write romance novel prose in Rachelle’s style and voice.

USER: Be RachAyalaFirstPovPres and write a romance short story with a twist.

ASSISTANT (this is written by the fine-tune model):

[First-person present tense, Raya’s point of view]

I have a knack for saving the most difficult for last. I scan the room of singles, all of them chatting, laughing, and having a good time. The women are all dressed up, while the men are in business casual, but not too casual. The DJ is playing soft rock and pop tunes, and everyone’s sipping on some kind of drink.

My gaze lands on a man sitting alone at the bar. I don’t know why I didn’t notice him before. He’s not a bad-looking guy. In fact, he’s quite attractive with his black hair, muscular build, and sharp jawline. He’s wearing a button-up shirt with the sleeves rolled up to his elbows, and he has a glass of water in front of him.

I take a deep breath and walk over to him. He glances at me but quickly looks away. He’s not interested, but that’s never stopped me before.

“Hi,” I say, taking the seat next to him.

“Hi,” he replies without looking at me.

I’m not one to give up so easily. I lean closer to him. “I’m Raya. What’s your name?”

“Derek,” he answers, still not making eye contact.

I try to catch his gaze. “So, Derek, why are you sitting here all alone?”

He finally looks at me. His eyes are a dark brown, and they’re cold. “I’m waiting for someone.”

My heart sinks. “Oh. I see.”

I stand up and return to the singles’ area. I can’t let one rejection get me down. Besides, I’m not the only one who’s striking out. I see several other women who are also getting turned down by the men.

I’m about to approach another man when the host calls for everyone’s attention. “Alright, everyone, it’s time for the first activity of the night. We’re going to play a little game I like to call Love Connection.”

A few people cheer while others groan. I fall into the latter category. I’ve played this game before, and it never ends well. But I can’t be the only one who’s a Debbie Downer. The host has a wheel with various activities written on it. He spins the wheel, and it lands on “blindfolded taste test.”

The host claps his hands together. “Alright, I need two volunteers to come up to the stage.”

A woman and a man raise their hands, and they walk up to the stage. The host hands them each a blindfold. “Now, the woman will be blindfolded, and the man will feed her three different types of food. She has to guess what they are.”

The host hands the man a plate of food, and he takes a bite of one of the items. “This is some kind of fruit. It’s sweet and juicy.”

The woman laughs. “That could be any fruit.”

He takes another bite. “It’s red.”

“Strawberry,” she guesses.

“Correct!” the host says. “Now, let’s move on to the next item.”

I watch as the man feeds the woman a piece of celery and a piece of carrot. She guesses them both correctly. The host congratulates them and hands them each a raffle ticket. I can’t help but feel a little jealous. It must be nice to have a connection with someone.

The host spins the wheel again, and it lands on “speed dating.” A few people groan, but I don’t mind speed dating. I’ve actually had some success with it. I grab my glass of wine and walk over to the speed dating area. I take a seat at one of the tables, and a man sits across from me.

“Hi, I’m Raya,” I say, holding out my hand.

“Hi, I’m Peter,” he replies, shaking my hand.

He seems nice enough. He has sandy blond hair and blue eyes. He’s wearing a polo shirt and khaki shorts. He’s not exactly my type, but I’m not going to be picky.

“So, Peter, what do you do?” I ask.

“I’m a physical therapist,” he answers. “I work with athletes.”

“That’s cool,” I say. “I work in marketing.”

We make small talk for a few minutes before the host blows the whistle. It’s time to move on to the next person. I rotate to the next table, and the man sitting across from me is the one who rejected me at the bar. Derek.

“Fancy meeting you here,” I say with a forced smile.

He chuckles. “I could say the same to you.”

We make awkward small talk for a few minutes before the whistle blows. It’s time to move on to the next person. The rest of the speed dating rounds go by in a blur. I meet a software engineer, a personal trainer, and a teacher. They’re all nice, but there’s no spark. I don’t feel that connection that everyone’s talking about.

After the last round of speed dating, the host announces that it’s time for the final activity of the night. “We’re going to play a little game I like to call Love Lockdown. Each woman will be handcuffed to a man for the next hour.”

The women cheer while the men groan. I can’t help but feel sorry for them. They have no say in who they’re handcuffed to. The host hands out the handcuffs, and we’re all paired up. I’m paired with the software engineer. He’s a nice guy, but there’s no spark.

I look over at Derek, who’s paired with a woman who’s practically hanging off of him. She’s giggling and twirling her hair, and he’s smiling at her. I feel a pang of jealousy, but I quickly push it aside. It’s not like I’m interested in him. I’m just competitive, and I don’t like losing.

I try to make the best of the situation. The software engineer and I play a few rounds of trivia, and we win a few raffle tickets. But the whole time, I can’t help but steal glances at Derek. He and his partner are having a grand old time. They’re laughing and whispering to each other, and he has his arm around her.

I glance at the clock on the wall. There are only a few minutes left of the game. I need to make a move if I want to win the grand prize. I don’t even know what the grand prize is, but I have to win it. I can’t let Derek beat me.

I lean over to the software engineer. “Do you mind if I take a bathroom break?”

He shrugs. “Sure, go ahead.”

I stand up and walk over to Derek and his partner. “Hey, guys, do you mind if I cut in for a few minutes?”

His partner looks at me with a raised eyebrow, but she hands me the handcuff key. “Be my guest.”

She stands up and takes the software engineer’s hand. “Let’s go get some drinks.”

Derek and I are left alone at the table. I can feel the tension between us. I don’t know why he’s getting to me so much. Maybe it’s the handcuffs. Or maybe it’s the fact that he rejected me earlier. I need to prove to him that I’m a catch.

“So, Derek, why did you come to a singles event if you’re waiting for someone?” I ask.

He shrugs. “I’m not waiting for anyone in particular. I’m just here to have a good time.”

I narrow my eyes at him. “Then why did you reject me earlier?”

He chuckles. “I didn’t reject you. I just told you I was waiting for someone.”

I roll my eyes. “Semantics. So, are you having a good time?”

He looks at me, and his gaze is intense. “I am now.”

I feel my face flush, and I quickly look away. I can’t let him see that he’s getting to me. I change the subject. “So, do you come to these events often?”

He shakes his head. “This is my first time. What about you?”

I shrug. “I’ve been to a few. They’re hit or miss.”

He smiles. “I’d say this one’s a hit.”

I can’t help but smile back. He’s charming, I’ll give him that. I look at the clock on the wall. There are only a few seconds left of the game. I need to make a move if I want to win the grand prize.

“Hey, Derek, do you want to be my partner for the grand prize?” I ask.

He raises an eyebrow. “What’s the grand prize?”

“I have no idea, but I have to win it,” I say. “I’m competitive like that.”

He laughs. “Alright, you’re on. What do we have to do?”

The host walks up to the stage. “Alright, everyone, it’s time to announce the winners of the grand prize. The winning couple is the one that has the most raffle tickets. So, let’s see who the lucky winners are.”

The host pulls a raffle ticket out of the bucket. “The winning couple has ten raffle tickets. Do we have any couples with ten raffle tickets?”

The teacher raises her hand. “We have ten raffle tickets!”

The host pulls another ticket out of the bucket. “The winning couple has eleven raffle tickets. Do we have any couples with eleven raffle tickets?”

The software engineer raises his hand. “We have eleven raffle tickets!”

I groan. I was so close to winning. I look over at Derek, but he only has six raffle tickets. There’s no way we can win. I slump in my chair, feeling defeated.

The host pulls one more ticket out of the bucket. “The winning couple has twelve raffle tickets. Do we have any couples with twelve raffle tickets?”

Derek and his partner raise their hands. “We have twelve raffle tickets!”

I can’t believe it. Derek won. I glare at him, but he only grins back at me. The host hands them the grand prize, which is a gift card to a fancy restaurant.

“Congratulations to Derek and his lovely partner!” the host says. “I hope you have a wonderful time on your date.”

Derek’s partner takes the gift card and gives him a hug. I roll my eyes. Of course, she’s going to fall for him. He’s tall, dark, and handsome. He’s charming and charismatic. He’s everything a woman could want.

I stand up and uncuff myself from the software engineer. “Thanks for a great time.”

He shrugs. “It was fun. Maybe we can do it again sometime.”

I force a smile. “Sure, I’ll see you around.”

I walk over to Derek and his partner. “Congratulations on winning the grand prize.”

“Thanks,” Derek says. “I have to give all the credit to my partner. She’s the real MVP.”

His partner giggles and twirls her hair. “Aw, thanks, Derek. You’re too sweet.”

I resist the urge to gag. They’re so nauseatingly cute. I can’t stand it. I need to get out of here before I lose my lunch. I grab my purse and make a beeline for the exit.

“Raya, wait!” Derek calls after me.

I ignore him and keep walking. I’m not going to give him the satisfaction of seeing me upset. I’m a strong, independent woman, and I don’t need a man to complete me.

I push open the door and step outside. The cool night air hits me, and I take a deep breath. I pull out my phone and order a rideshare. I’m about to put my phone away when I get a notification. It’s a message from Derek.

Derek: Raya, wait. I want to talk to you.

I roll my eyes and type out a reply.

Raya: There’s nothing to talk about. You won. Congratulations. Have a great time on your date.

I put my phone away and cross my arms. A few minutes later, my rideshare pulls up. I climb into the backseat and sink down in my seat. I close my eyes and let out a deep breath. I can’t believe I let Derek get to me. I barely know him, and yet, I’m so hung up on him. I need to get over it and move on.

My phone pings with another message from Derek. I ignore it and put my phone on silent. I lean my head against the window and watch the city lights pass by. I’m lost in my thoughts when the driver pulls up to my apartment building. I thank him and climb out of the car.

I take the elevator up to my floor and unlock my apartment door. I kick off my heels and flop down on the couch. I stare up at the ceiling, feeling sorry for myself. I’m about to reach for a pint of ice cream when I hear a knock on the door. I glance at the clock. It’s almost midnight. Who could be knocking on my door at this hour?

I walk over to the door and peer through the peephole. It’s Derek. What is he doing here? I debate whether or not to open the door. I should be strong and tell him to leave me alone. But my curiosity gets the better of me, and I unlock the door.

“Derek, what are you doing here?” I ask.

He holds up his phone. “I got a notification that you read my message, but you didn’t reply. I wanted to make sure you got home okay.”

I raise an eyebrow. “You wanted to make sure I got home okay? Or did you just want to rub it in my face that you won?”

He winces. “Ouch. I deserved that. I’m sorry if I came on too strong. I just wanted to have a good time, and I thought you did too.”

I sigh. “I did have a good time. Until you won the grand prize with your partner.”

He steps closer to me. “She’s not my partner. You are.”

I frown. “What do you mean? I thought the grand prize was the gift card to the fancy restaurant.”

He shakes his head. “That’s not the real grand prize. The real grand prize is finding a connection with someone. And I found that connection with you.”

I feel my heart flutter. “You did? Even though we only met tonight?”

He nods. “I know it sounds crazy, but I can’t stop thinking about you. I felt something when we were talking. It was like we had this instant connection. And I want to see where it goes.”

I take a step closer to him. “I felt it too. But what about your partner? She seemed pretty into you.”

He shrugs. “I’m not interested in her. I’m interested in you. So, what do you say? Will you go out with me?”

I look into his warm brown eyes, and I see the sincerity in them. I take a deep breath and make a decision. “Yes. I’d love to go out with you.”

He grins and takes my hand. “Great. How about tomorrow night? I’ll take you to that fancy restaurant with the gift card.”

I chuckle. “I’d like that. But I have to warn you, I have expensive taste.”

He smiles. “I can afford it. For you, it’s worth it.”

I feel my cheeks flush, and I look down at my feet. He reaches out and tilts my chin up so that I’m looking into his eyes.

“Raya, I know we just met, but I have a good feeling about this. I think you’re someone special, and I don’t want to let you go.”

I smile, feeling a warmth spread through me. “I think you’re pretty special too. I’m excited to see where this goes.”

He leans in, and I close my eyes. Our lips meet in a soft, sweet kiss. It’s like magic. I feel that spark everyone’s talking about. It’s like we were meant to be together. I know it sounds crazy, but sometimes, you just have to take a chance on love.

And that’s exactly what I’m going to do.

[/First-person present tense, Raya’s point of view]

It’s not the best writing, but at least it doesn’t sound like ChatGPT, and that’s the point of the fine tune. One thing I notice is that all the dialogue is tagged, whereas my writing has more untagged dialogue to keep the scene moving. This could mean that I’ve made things too simple in that my user prompt didn’t give the LLM any guidance about the style or voice of the scene it is writing.

Another thing I noticed is repetitive sentence structure. Subject verse, subject verse. This is a problem of fine tunes in that they can become habituated to a particular style and not break loose. One reason is that we lowered both the Temperature and the TopP down from 1.0 to 0.7.

Did you notice it lost narrative logic? I could have sworn that Raya cut in and became Derek’s partner for the raffle ticket game, but somehow, she was back with the software engineer. Also, the host announced the winning couple three times, but this could just be a feature of the dating game. Nevertheless, these discrepancies show why AI (or at least the not-so-smart models like GPT-3.5) need to be edited and fact-checked.

WRITING STYLE GUIDED FIRST-PERSON POV

Since the previous fine-tuning missed the mark, I decided to add more information to the user prompt. After all, I didn’t tell it what writing style to use to write the scene. This time, I’m going to add information to the user prompt.

Since I need to enter “style information” into the user prompt, I’ll need two passes through my writing samples.

In the first step, I’ll ask the LLM to describe the writing style. I use the same one I’m going to fine tune. After all, that LLM’s vocabulary is what I’m interested in.

Step 1:

Writing Style Description Prompt: Please analyze the writing style, tone, and voice and describe it in a paragraph of 300 words. Be sure to cover pacing, dialogue style, descriptive language, emotional tone, sentence structure, and vocabulary and diction.

Collect all of these descriptions, and DO NOT EDIT them. This is what the LLM thinks. What we’re trying to do is to train the LLM with its own description of writing style so that the results match and make sense for that particular LLM.

Step 2:

Create the fine-tune dataset with the following prompts. [You may modify to fit your use.]

SYSTEM: You are a creative writer able to write romance novel prose to match a given writing style.

USER: Write romance novel prose in the writing style: {insert style description collected in step 1}

ASSISTANT: {insert the corresponding excerpt}

Result Two:

Here is a romantic scene my fine-tune wrote (Temperature: 0.7, TopP: 0.7)

SYSTEM: You are a creative writer able to write romance novel prose to match a given writing style.

USER: Write a sweet romance short story in the writing style: {insert style description from one of the scenes}

ASSISTANT: (what follows below)

[Brynn]

“Marry me, Brynn.”

I freeze, the buttercream-covered spatula hanging in mid-air. Did I hear him right? I turn around, and there’s Harrison, down on one knee, holding a small, black velvet box open.

He’s grinning from ear to ear, his dimples on full display. His eyes are shining with so much love, and my heart melts right along with the buttercream in my hand.

“Harrison.” I can’t even get out the words. I’m so surprised, I don’t know what to say. Or do. Or think. Or breathe.

Is this really happening? Or am I hallucinating? Because this has got to be a dream come true. My dream. The one I never dared to dream because I never thought it could come true.

But here he is, my boyfriend, my man, my Harrison, with a ring in his hand, asking me to marry him. I’ve been waiting for this moment for so long, and now that it’s here, I’m completely at a loss for words.

He stands up, still grinning, and takes my buttercream-covered hand in his. “I love you, Brynn. I’ve loved you from the moment I first saw you. You’re the most amazing woman I’ve ever met, and you’re my best friend. I can’t imagine my life without you. Will you marry me?”

Tears fill my eyes, and my heart swells so much I’m afraid it might burst. “Oh, Harrison. I love you so much. Of course, I’ll marry you.”

He slips the ring on my finger, and it fits perfectly. It’s a simple, elegant, round-cut diamond in a platinum setting. Just like Harrison, it’s understated, classic, and beautiful.

I fling my arms around his neck, and he pulls me close, his mouth finding mine. I melt into him, kissing him with all the love and passion in my heart. I never want this moment to end.

But it does, all too soon, because my phone is ringing. I groan, and Harrison chuckles. “Let me guess. That’s your mom, calling for the hundredth time today.”

I glance at the phone screen. “Yup. She wants to know how the cake tasting is going.”

He laughs. “I’d better get back to work. I’m sure my mom’s calling me, too. I’m supposed to be picking out the tuxedos.”

“Right. The tuxedos. I guess we should start planning the wedding, huh?”

He grins. “I can’t wait to marry you, Brynn. I love you so much.”

“I love you, too, Harrison.”

We kiss one more time, and then he goes back to the kitchen, and I finish frosting the cake. I’m floating on a cloud of happiness, so happy I can’t stop grinning. I’m going to marry the man of my dreams. I’m going to be Mrs. Harrison Bailey.

My phone rings again. I glance at the screen, and it’s my best friend, Zoe. I pick up. “Hey, girl. You’ll never guess what just happened.”

“What? What? What?” she screeches in my ear. “Did he propose?”

“Yes!” I squeal. “He proposed, and I said yes!”

“Oh my God, I’m so happy for you. How did he do it? Did he get down on one knee? Did he cry? Did you cry?”

I laugh. “Yes, he got down on one knee, and no, he didn’t cry. But I did. I’m such a sap.”

“Of course you cried. You’re such a romantic. Oh, I can’t wait to see the ring. Send me a picture. Wait, let me call your sister first. She’s going to be so jealous.”

I groan. “Don’t tell her yet. I want to tell her myself.”

“Fine. I’ll call her after you tell me all the juicy details. When’s the wedding? What’s the date? Have you started planning yet? Oh my God, this is so exciting.”

“Whoa, whoa, slow down. He just proposed. We haven’t even set a date yet.”

“Are you going to have a big wedding or a small one? Do you want me to be your maid of honor? Are you going to ask your sister?”

“I don’t know, Zoe. It just happened. I need to talk to Harrison first. We have to figure out what we both want.”

“Okay, okay, I’ll stop bombarding you with questions. I’m just so excited for you.”

“I’m excited, too. I’m going to marry the man of my dreams.”

“You mean the man of your lists?”

I laugh. “Yes, the man of my lists. My lists worked, Zoe. I got everything I ever wanted.”

“I’m so happy for you, Brynn. You deserve it. You’ve been through so much. And I know your parents would be so proud of you.”

I blink back tears. I still miss my parents every day. They were the best parents in the world, and they loved me so much. I wish they could be here to see this, to see me so happy.

“I know they’re watching over me,” I say. “And I know they’re happy for me.”

“I know they are. They’re probably planning the wedding in heaven.”

I giggle. “I bet they are. They’re probably arguing over what kind of cake we should have.”

“I’m so glad you found Harrison. He’s perfect for you. He’s so patient and understanding, and he really loves you.”

“I love him, too. He’s everything I ever wanted in a man.”

“Have you told him about the lists yet?”

“No. Not yet. I will, though. I think it’s time.”

“Good. You need to be honest with him. It’s not fair to keep secrets. I’m sure he’ll understand.”

I sigh. “I hope so. I know he’s the one for me. I just don’t want to mess things up.”

“You won’t mess things up. You’ve both grown so much, and you’ve been through so much together. You have a strong foundation. You’ll be fine.”

“I hope so. I don’t want to lose him.”

“You won’t. Just be honest with him. You’ll see. Everything will be okay.”

“Thanks, Zoe. I’m so glad I have you in my life.”

“Aw, I love you, too, Brynn. Now, spill. How did he propose? I want all the details.”

I smile, feeling like the luckiest woman in the world. “He proposed at the bakery. He got down on one knee while I was frosting a cake, and he told me how much he loved me and how he couldn’t imagine his life without me. And then he asked me to marry him.”

“That’s so sweet. And so perfect. I’m so happy for you.”

“I’m happy, too. I can’t wait to start planning the wedding.”

“Ooh, are you going to be a bridezilla?”

I laugh. “I hope not. I want everything to be perfect, but I don’t want to be one of those crazy brides. I just want to enjoy the process and make sure everything is exactly the way I want it.”

“Of course, you do. You’re Brynn. You have to have everything your way.”

I stick my tongue out at her, even though she can’t see me. “Shut up. I’m not that bad.”

“Uh-huh. Sure, you’re not. You know, you could always use the lists for planning the wedding. List everything you want, and then prioritize them. It’s the perfect way to make sure you get everything you want.”

I groan. “I’m not going to let you live that down, am I?”

“Not a chance. I’m going to remind you every chance I get. You have to admit, the lists worked.”

I roll my eyes. “Fine, fine. The lists worked. Happy now?”

“Ecstatic. I can’t wait to see you walk down the aisle and say ‘I do.’”

“I can’t wait, either. I’m going to be Mrs. Harrison Bailey. It’s a dream come true.”

“I’m so happy for you, Brynn. You deserve all the happiness in the world.”

“Thanks, Zoe. I love you, girl.”

“I love you, too. Now, go call your sister. She’s going to be so excited for you.”

“Okay, okay. I’ll call her. Talk to you later.”

I hang up and stare at the ring on my finger. I can’t believe I’m engaged. I can’t believe I’m going to marry Harrison. I can’t believe I’m going to be Mrs. Harrison Bailey.

I’m so happy, I can’t stop grinning. I finish frosting the cake, and then I take a picture of it and text it to Harrison.

The cake looks delicious, he texts back. Can’t wait to eat it.

Me, too. I can’t wait to be your wife, I text back.

I can’t wait to make you mine, he texts.

[/Brynn]

This sample has many more untagged dialogue samples, which are in my style. I think adding the writing style guidance made the LLM understand a little more of what snappy dialogue means. It still tends to use the same sentence structure, and it loses narrative logic. But I didn’t provide a scene brief or plan, so the LLM winged it. Besides, under the hood, it is still GPT-3.5, even though it no longer writes like ChatGPT.

I’ll use it for a few days and see how I like it, but I believe I found a way to make a fine tune without the lexical analysis and concordance work that gives you the very best fine tunes. For that, please see the video from Future Fiction Academy. “How to Build a Fine Tune for Fiction: Tips & Tricks” (https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ctNys4Jl6ME) ⁠1

Future Fiction Academy Rexy has an “LLM Tuner” (https://rexy.futurefictionacademy.com/LLM_Tuner ⁠2 ) where you can enter your System, User, and Assistant messages in text boxes. It will generate a JSONL file. You can also load from CSV and edit an existing JSONL file. Then, you can save and download the new JSONL file and put it into the OpenAI fine-tune page. (Rexy requires a membership at the FFA.)

​[ ​PART 7​ ]​

YOUR AI-ENABLED SECOND BRAIN

​[ ​38​ ]​

WHY YOU NEED AN AI-ENABLED SECOND BRAIN

If you’re like me and you’ve written one or many books, you’ve often wished to have a second brain—a way to organize your books, series, characters, and plots in a way where you can easily retrieve information. You might vaguely remember that a particular clue was hidden in plain sight but can’t find the location, or you’ve forgotten the eye color of a minor character.

Some of you were organized and provided breadcrumbs to yourself through character spreadsheets, plot summaries, and world-building lore books. However, no matter how meticulous you were, there are details you never thought you’d need ten books down, and now you’re doing word searches through your manuscript to find the passage and context.

Others have put everything into databases or organized Scrivener files, Notion pages, and every other tool. However, there’s a big problem.

By nature, you had to pick and choose what you thought was relevant at the time to record. I mean, you’re not going to put in a walk-in character or an event meant to add humor or color to a scene. And that’s the trouble with most second-brain schemes.

Wouldn’t you like to have an expert who can suck in your entire novel or even your whole series and be able to answer questions accurately—and not just general questions, but find that needle in the haystack and then go to the place and show it to you? How about a series expert who can not only tell you about your details but also suggest characters and plot lines to expand your series in ways that will delight your readers?

How about a brain that can pull together plot threads spread across large distances? Perhaps this walk-on character was only mentioned in three places far apart but held the clue that solved the mystery. Or there’s a piece of arcane magic that was foreshadowed five books back, and there are glimmers of its power, but no actual plot turns around it. This world expert will be fluent in any language, magic, cultural traditions, and the taxonomy of your characters and social and physical systems. It can keep track of everything and suggest the evolution of your world or the development of new technologies. Imagine if Tolkien had such a world-keeper.

The possibilities are endless. You can even give abandoned manuscripts to this Second Brainiac Story Doctor and have it suggest ways to fix up your story, and of course, you can have it help you with your work in progress.

Get excited because today’s AI LLMs can give you a “living” second brain. And no, it’s not as hyped as it was a few months ago, before Google released Gemini 1.5 Pro, a sparse mixture-of-experts multimodal LLM capable of recalling and reasoning across a million words.

Take a breath.

Before I talk about Gemini Pro 1.5’s capabilities, let’s go back to the recent past and the limitations of traditional tools and specially designed long-context window LLMs that use Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG).

THE LIMITATIONS OF TRADITIONAL STORY OR SERIES BLUEPRINT TOOLS

A month ago, when I was planning this book, I had a list of tools I would talk about. The usual suspects are AI-enhanced Notion and special applications like Novelcrafter, which has a Codex where you can store story information. I was going to talk about large-at-the-time-context-window LLMs like Claude 3 (200k tokens), GPT4 (128K tokens), and mention methods of uploading one chapter at a time and having AI summarize and pull out characters, settings, events, actions and put them in documents.

However, all of these methods had one big red flag. What was NOT saved is lost. Obvious, right? Summarization necessarily takes what was deemed necessary at the time and loses the rest of the information. The main characters are saved. Their motivation and goals are summarized. Settings turn into one-liners. Richness is lost.

Late last year, LLMs were released with an improvement called Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG). A lot of us got excited. It was supposed to retrieve needles in haystacks and offer a glimmer of hope for authors seeking a more efficient and reliable way to manage their creative work.

Unfortunately for authors but not for other applications, RAG relies on summaries and extracted keywords, which proved disappointing for fiction writers because it failed at providing detailed chapter-by-chapter outlines.

The problem with RAG is that information is lost in summarization, just like when you manually update your spreadsheets and second-brain databases. RAG typically uses keyword extraction or summarization techniques to create a condensed version of your work. This process is similar to how a SparkNotes summary can’t capture the full richness of a classic novel.

Here’s how missing details can impact your writing:

Plot Holes and Inconsistencies: Forgetting or overlooking details can lead to plot holes, where events don’t follow logically or contradict previously established information.

Character Inconsistencies: If the AI doesn’t have access to the complete picture of a character’s development, it might generate content that contradicts their established personality, motivations, or relationships. This can make characters feel inconsistent and unbelievable.

World-Building Errors: Missing details about the world’s history, geography, culture, or magic system can lead to inconsistencies and confusion. This can weaken the world-building and make it difficult for readers to immerse themselves in the story fully.

While RAG can be helpful for some tasks, it’s not ideal for maintaining consistency and continuity in complex narratives. Native large context models like Gemini 1.5 Pro, which can directly analyze and understand the full text of your work, offer a more reliable solution for authors who want to ensure the accuracy and consistency of their fictional universes.

WHY I’M IN LOVE WITH GEMINI 1.5 PRO

Imagine you have a friend who reads tons of books and remembers every detail, even from years ago. Furthermore, your bookworm friend can come up with new insights based on the content of your books and she’s always ready to brainstorm and analyze, day or night. Wait no longer, because Gemini 1.5 Pro is here.

Here are her capabilities in a nutshell:

  • She can hold your books up to a million tokens or 750,000 words in her memory in total, not in part, and she can retrieve information, no matter how obscure it is and where it’s tucked. She has perfect “needle in a haystack” retrieval of up to 530,000 tokens or approximately 400,000 words and 99.7% retrieval of up to a million tokens or 750,000 words.

  • She doesn’t need to cram or study summaries or snippets of your work because Gemini 1.5 Pro can read and understand your entire book or series.

  • She can also learn in context, meaning she is not relying on her training dataset to pull together concepts. This means she can reason with you about your work in progress or across your entire series, even if it is not yet published and is unknown in her training dataset.

  • Because she is multimodal, you can upload photographs, images, maps, videos, and other material into your personal knowledge base. She can read maps, plan road trips for your characters, and even suggest a wardrobe based on a combination of your descriptions and the images you uploaded.

  • She never sleeps. Ask anything, anytime. Forgot a character’s eye color from book one? Need to check if a plot point in book five contradicts something from book two? No problem! Worried that your character is acting inconsistently? She can point it out and also suggest why your character, who was shy in book 1, is now a public speaker in book 5.

Okay, I’m sure you’re dying to try it out. Here is the URL: https://aistudio.google.com ⁠1

Here is an article to help you understand the capabilities of utilizing the entire context window without using RAG: “Gemini 1.5: Unlocking multimodal understanding across millions of tokens of context” (https://storage.googleapis.com/deepmind-media/gemini/gemini_v1_5_report.pdf) ⁠2

​[ ​39​ ]​

USE CASES FOR YOUR SECOND BRAIN

The first use case is to use Gemini 1.5 Pro to generate a story or series blueprint. She can easily create a list of characters, plot points, and settings, giving you a clear overview of your story’s structure.

Once you have your generated Story Blueprint, you should immediately review it while the details are still fresh in your mind. Gemini, like other Language Models (LLMs), is a generative tool and not a data retrieval system, so she might make up information or introduce inconsistencies. Correct anything wrong before putting the information into your content management system.

However, Gemini’s capabilities extend far beyond generating a Story Blueprint. One of the significant advantages of using Gemini is her ability to answer questions about the generated content. If you come across any questionable information in the Story Blueprint, you can ask Gemini to clarify and tell you which chapter she got the purported information from. This is possible because the entire book or series remains within Gemini’s context window.

While Gemini 1.5 Pro can easily provide you with a Story Blueprint so you can see your story at a glance, that’s not all she can do. Oh no, she’s capable of reaching into greater depth than a mere list of characters, plot points, and settings.

Gemini 1.5 Pro can help you with unpublished works because of her ability to learn from the information placed inside her context window. You can upload several documents. Imagine uploading not only your work in progress but perhaps articles consisting of research or genre-specific plot structures. Since I’m the author of Romance in a Month or Dangerous Love: Writing a Romantic Suspense, I can upload a copy of my book as a guidebook along with my work in progress and Gemini will look across these documents to help me apply the principles of one book to the next.

She can act as a Story Doctor or a critique partner. I can upload a style guide, for example, and query my book against a publishing house’s style guide. Even better, any prompts or ideas I suggest in the conversation are worked into Gemini’s context memory and incorporated into future reasoning and responses.

I can have a critique partner who refines her critiques by listening to my explanations and comparing them with my work in progress and research materials, as well as any writing books I use as references.

WORK IN PROGRESS ANALYSIS AND SUGGESTIONS

Example conversations with Gemini 1.5 Pro from my Work in Progress: Not My Bridegroom ⁠1 , a romantic comedy where an internet influencer has to use her ex-boyfriend as a deepfake in her wedding planning videos.

<Conversation>

USER:

Please suggest specific scenes to improve romantic tension between Dillon and Anita.

MODEL:

Scenes to Enhance Romantic Tension:

1. Vulnerable Confessions:

Setting: After the mugging incident, Anita and Dillon are alone in her apartment. The atmosphere is charged with emotion and unspoken feelings.

Action: Anita opens up to Dillon about her insecurities and doubts about her relationship with Eduardo. Dillon, in turn, confesses his lingering feelings for her and his hurt over their past misunderstanding. They share a tender moment of connection and understanding.

2. Stolen Moments amidst Chaos:

Setting: During a chaotic wedding planning event with Eduardo present, Anita and Dillon find themselves alone in a secluded corner of the venue (e.g., a garden, a balcony, a quiet room).

Action: Amidst the stress and pressure, they share a stolen moment of intimacy. A lingering look, a brush of hands, or a whispered conversation conveys their unspoken desire for one another.

3. A Dance of Desire:

Setting: At a social gathering or a club, Dillon and Anita find themselves on the dance floor. The music is slow and sensual, creating an intimate atmosphere.

Action: As they dance, their bodies move in sync, and their eyes lock. The tension builds as they are drawn closer, their movements becoming more intimate and suggestive.

4. A Moment of Comfort:

Setting: After a particularly challenging encounter with Eduardo, Anita is feeling vulnerable and upset. She seeks out Dillon for comfort and support.

Action: Dillon offers a listening ear and a shoulder to cry on. He provides words of encouragement and reassurance, reminding Anita of her strength and worth. Their connection deepens as they find solace in each other’s presence.

5. A Playful Challenge:

Setting: During a casual outing or activity (e.g., a picnic, a game night), Dillon and Anita engage in a playful competition.

Action: The competition becomes charged with flirtation and suggestive banter. The stakes are raised as they challenge each other, creating a sense of excitement and anticipation.

Additional Tips:

Utilize Sensory Details: Describe the physical sensations and emotions experienced by the characters, such as the warmth of their touch, the scent of their cologne, and the racing of their hearts.

Build Anticipation: Gradually escalate the tension through suggestive dialogue, lingering glances, and close proximity.

Create Obstacles: Introduce external factors that prevent them from acting on their feelings, heightening the sense of longing and desire.

Use Internal Monologues: Reveal the characters’ inner thoughts and desires, allowing readers to understand the depth of their emotions.

By incorporating these scene suggestions and focusing on building emotional intimacy, you can create a captivating romance between Anita and Dillon that will leave readers yearning for more.

</Conversation>

What Gemini did here was take specific scenes and suggest enhancements. These enhancements were not simply retrievals of what happened in the scene; using her reasoning capabilities about romantic tension, she added possible extensions of existing scenes.

I’m very open to sharing my work in progress, but I have added a disclaimer. I may or may not incorporate any of these suggestions, and since I’m a complete pantser, I don’t actually know the ending or whether any of these suggestions will play out or not.

I only included this to show you the power of Gemini Pro 1.5. Continuing …

<Conversation>

USER:

Please point out any places where Wanda acts out of her usual character.

MODEL:

Instances of Wanda Acting Out of Character:

While Wanda is generally portrayed as cynical, sarcastic, and distrustful of men, there are a few instances where her actions seem to deviate from her established personality:

Chapter 16: Encouraging the Fake Romance: During the Napa trip, Wanda actively participates in creating a romantic atmosphere for Anita and Dillon, despite her usual skepticism of love and relationships. She directs them to act affectionate and even encourages them to kiss for the camera. This behavior contradicts her typical cynicism and suggests a softer side that emerges when she sees genuine connection and happiness between Anita and Dillon.

Chapter 17: Offering to Hack Cookie’s Account: In response to Cookie’s online rant, Wanda suggests hacking her account and deleting the posts. While this aligns with her tech-savvy nature, it seems out of character for her to take such a drastic and potentially illegal action, especially as it involves deceiving and manipulating someone she knows.

Chapter 18: Inviting Dillon to the Club: At the cafe, Wanda joins Gina and Heidi in inviting Dillon to their girls’ night out. This seems uncharacteristic given her usual aversion to male company and her protectiveness over Anita. Her motivation might be to further observe Dillon and his intentions or to create more drama for the vlog.

Possible Explanations:

Character Development: Wanda’s actions could indicate a gradual shift in her perspective as she witnesses the genuine connection between Anita and Dillon. Their relationship might challenge her cynicism and open her up to the possibility of love and trust.

Hidden Motivations: Wanda might have ulterior motives for her actions, such as wanting to protect Anita from further harm by Eduardo or creating more drama for the vlog to boost its popularity.

Inconsistency in Characterization: There might be some inconsistencies in how Wanda’s character is portrayed throughout the story. It’s important to ensure her actions and reactions remain consistent with her established personality and motivations.

</Conversation>

Wow, is that powerful or not?

CHARACTER INTERVIEW

Following that analysis, I decided to interview Anita, my main character.

<Conversation>

USER:

Anita, what is it you really want deep inside?

MODEL:

Deep inside, what I truly crave is a love that feels real, a connection that goes beyond the superficiality of likes, follows, and perfectly curated Instagram posts.

I long for someone who sees me for who I am, flaws and all, and loves me anyway. Someone who makes me laugh, challenges me, and supports my dreams. A partner who is present, both physically and emotionally, someone I can share my deepest thoughts and fears with, without judgment.

I want a love that feels like coming home, a safe haven where I can be myself without the pressure of performing or maintaining a perfect image. A love that is built on trust, honesty, and mutual respect.

I want the kind of love that Dillon offers, a love that feels effortless and genuine, a love that makes my heart soar even in the midst of chaos.

USER:

Why are you still hung up on Eduardo?

MODEL:

I’m ashamed to admit it, but a part of me is still drawn to Eduardo because of the status and validation he represents.

He’s the epitome of success in the tech world, the handsome billionaire everyone admires. Being with him elevates my social standing and fuels my influencer career.

There’s a certain thrill in being associated with someone so powerful and influential. It feeds my ego and satisfies my desire for recognition and external validation.

And honestly, I’m afraid of letting go of that. I’m scared of starting over, of losing the lifestyle I’ve grown accustomed to, and of facing the uncertainty of building a life with someone like Dillon who isn’t a guaranteed success story.

It’s a shallow and insecure part of myself that I’m struggling to overcome.

USER:

But you do know that Dillon will be hurt, even though you think he understands why you’re doing what you’re doing. How will you react if Dillon decides he’s had enough?

MODEL:

The thought of Dillon walking away fills me with dread. I know deep down that he deserves better than to be a pawn in this charade.

If he decides he’s had enough, I’ll be heartbroken. I’ll finally have to confront the reality that I’ve pushed away the one person who truly cares for me, all for the sake of a superficial and ultimately meaningless relationship with Eduardo.

I’ll have to face the consequences of my actions and the emptiness of a life built on likes and follows. And the worst part is, I’ll know that I only have myself to blame.

USER:

Then how can you fix this?

MODEL:

Fixing this mess won’t be easy, but I know I have to start by being honest with myself and with those around me.

GENRE-SPECIFIC AI RESEARCH AND PROMPTS

ROMANCE

I’ve written several nonfiction books on how to write romances, so I’m going to use my books as a knowledge base and put them into the Gemini 1.5 Pro context window. To do that, I’ll go to Google’s AI Studio https://aistudio.google.com/ ⁠1

1. Upload the entire PDF of Rachelle Ayala’s Romance in a Month into the Gemini 1.5 Pro AI Studio. Upload the entire PDF of Rachelle Ayala’s 366 Ways to Know Your Character.

2. Reduce the Safety Settings by sliding them down to none.

Here is an example conversation.

USER: Please give me a process for writing a romance.

MODEL:

Writing a Romance: A Step-by-Step Guide

Here’s a process for crafting your own captivating romance novel:

1. Character Development:

Choose Archetypes: Start with classic archetypes like the “Bad Boy” or “Boss Lady” for your hero and heroine. This provides a foundation for their personalities.

Develop Goals and Motivations: Flesh out your characters by giving them clear goals and motivations. What do they desire most? Why do they want it? Make sure their goals conflict to create tension.

Internal Conflicts: Give each character an internal conflict stemming from a positive trait, creating complexity and driving emotional engagement. For example, a protective hero might become overly suspicious, causing tension with the heroine.

2. Central Conflict and Plot Points:

Core Conflict: The central conflict should be relational and internal, challenging their core beliefs and values. For instance, a career-driven heroine might clash with a laid-back hero, creating tension and driving the story.

The Meet: Create a memorable “meet-cute” early in the story, sparking initial attraction and hinting at the core conflict.

Lock-In: Devise a situation that forces the hero and heroine to interact regularly, such as working together or being part of the same social circle.

Main Conflict Escalation: Introduce challenges and obstacles stemming from the core conflict, testing the relationship and creating tension.

Realization Point: One or both characters acknowledge their feelings, raising the stakes and intensifying the push and pull of the relationship.

Big Bad Breakup (Optional): Consider a dramatic breakup fueled by the core conflict, forcing characters to confront their internal struggles.

Grand Romantic Moment: a memorable scene where the couple overcomes their challenges and reconciles. Make it sweet, emotional, and satisfying.

3. Additional Considerations:

Point of View: Choose between first-person (from the heroine’s or both characters’ perspectives) or third-person narration.

Heat Level: Determine the level of sensuality and intimacy you want in your story.

Subplots (Limited): Keep subplots minimal to avoid diluting the main romance and maintain focus.

4. Revision and Publication:

Revision: Revise and polish your draft, exploring subplots and refining character development and plot points.

Editing: Seek professional editing to ensure a high-quality manuscript.

Publishing: Decide between traditional or self-publishing and explore the necessary steps, such as finding an agent or designing a cover.

Remember: This is a flexible framework. Adapt it to your unique story and characters. Embrace creativity and have fun bringing your romance to life!

(This information comes directly from my book.)

USER: Please analyze my story Not My Bridegroom and give me a detailed critique.

MODEL:

Not My Bridegroom: A Detailed Critique

Strengths:

Strong Voice and Characterization: Anita’s voice is distinct and engaging, with her sassy and sarcastic inner dialogue creating a humorous and relatable character. The supporting characters, particularly Wanda and Gina, add depth and humor with their contrasting personalities and perspectives.

Compelling Premise: The concept of a fake engagement turning into a real love triangle is intriguing and offers plenty of potential for conflict and drama. The exploration of social media influencer culture and the impact of AI on relationships adds a contemporary edge to the story.

Humor and Romance: The story effectively balances humor and romance, with witty banter and steamy scenes creating a satisfying read. The tension between Anita and Dillon is palpable, making their interactions both entertaining and emotionally engaging.

Themes: The story explores relevant themes such as the superficiality of social media, the challenges of maintaining authenticity in a curated online world, and the complexities of modern relationships.

Areas for Improvement:

Pacing: The story could benefit from a tighter pace, particularly in the first half. Some scenes, such as the extended descriptions of clothing and décor, could be trimmed or streamlined to keep the plot moving forward.

Eduardo’s Character: Eduardo feels somewhat one-dimensional as the stereotypical controlling and arrogant billionaire. Adding more depth and nuance to his character could make the conflict with Dillon more compelling and believable. Exploring his motivations and backstory could help humanize him beyond the “villain” archetype.

Anita’s Internal Conflict: While Anita’s internal struggle between her desire for fame and her growing feelings for Dillon is evident, it could be further explored. Delving deeper into her insecurities and motivations for pursuing the influencer lifestyle could add emotional depth and complexity to her character arc.

Resolution: The story ends on a cliffhanger, leaving the reader uncertain about Anita’s ultimate decision and the future of her relationships with both Dillon and Eduardo. While this can create anticipation for a sequel, it may leave some readers feeling unsatisfied without a clearer resolution to the central conflict.

Additional Suggestions:

Explore the Ethical Implications of AI: The story touches on the potential dangers of AI in matchmaking, but this theme could be further developed. Exploring the ethical implications of deepfake technology and the manipulation of reality could add depth and intrigue to the narrative.

Develop the Supporting Characters: While Wanda and Gina are entertaining, they could be further developed with their own storylines and challenges. This would enrich the overall narrative and provide additional perspectives on the central conflict.

Consider the Ending: While a cliffhanger can be effective, consider offering a more conclusive ending that resolves the main conflict while leaving room for future possibilities. This could involve Anita making a clear choice between Dillon and Eduardo, or perhaps finding a way to forge her own path outside of the expectations placed upon her by both men.

Overall, Not My Bridegroom is an engaging and entertaining read with strong characters and a compelling premise. Addressing the pacing and character development issues, along with exploring the themes more deeply, could elevate the story to its full potential.

Possible Resolution using Romance Conventions:

Confrontation and Resolution with Eduardo:

Anita, with the support of Dillon and her friends, gathers evidence of Eduardo’s manipulative behavior and the flaws in the LoveBytes algorithm. This could involve uncovering data manipulation or highlighting the negative experiences of other users.

Armed with this information, Anita confronts Eduardo, exposing his unethical practices and the true nature of their relationship. She threatens to expose him publicly unless he releases her from the contract and forgives her father’s debt.

Public Revelation and Happily Ever After:

The truth about Anita and Eduardo’s fake relationship is eventually revealed to the public, either through a carefully orchestrated media campaign or a dramatic exposé. Anita takes control of the narrative, exposing Eduardo’s manipulation and reclaiming her own identity.

Anita and Dillon’s relationship blossoms, their shared experiences and genuine connection leading to a deep and lasting love. They could even collaborate on a new project together, combining Anita’s writing skills with Dillon’s acting talent to create something authentic and meaningful.

The story concludes with a satisfying happily ever after, with Anita and Dillon finding love and success on their own terms. This could involve a beautiful wedding ceremony, planned by Cookie, or perhaps a more intimate commitment ceremony that reflects their unique bond.

Additional Considerations:

The Role of Social Media: Explore how Anita navigates the aftermath of the scandal on social media. Will she continue as an influencer, or will she choose a different path?

Character Growth: Show how both Anita and Dillon grow and mature throughout the story, learning from their mistakes and becoming stronger individuals.

Themes of Forgiveness and Redemption: Emphasize the importance of forgiveness and second chances, not only for Anita and Dillon but also for other characters who might have made mistakes.

By incorporating these missing plot points and following a classic romance structure, you can create a satisfying and emotionally resonant conclusion to Not My Bridegroom. The key is to focus on character development, authentic relationships, and the triumph of love over superficiality and deceit.

Here are three questions with potential answers to help develop a humorous romantic suspense heroine:

Question 13: What is an emotional blind spot for your character? Which person in her life reminds her to watch for it?

Answer: Your heroine’s blind spot could be her inability to recognize sarcasm. She takes everything literally, leading to humorous misunderstandings and awkward situations, especially during tense moments in the investigation. Her best friend, a sarcastic and witty individual, constantly reminds her to read between the lines, often with exasperated sighs and eye rolls.

Question 21: If your character were offered the wealth of the entire world for the life of a single child, one she was not related to and suffered from a disease, which would she choose? Would she regret her choice? What if it were the life of the man she loves? For example, he jumps in the ocean to save a juvenile delinquent?

Answer: Despite her quirkiness, your heroine has a strong moral compass. She would refuse the wealth, unable to bear the guilt of sacrificing a child’s life, even for all the riches in the world. She might initially struggle with the decision, tempted by the possibilities, but ultimately choose compassion. However, if it were the life of the man she loves, the choice would become agonizing, creating an internal conflict between her love and her morals. This internal struggle could be a source of humor, as she debates the pros and cons in her unique, literal way, while also highlighting the depth of her love and the lengths she’d go to for the man she loves.

Question 28: Has your character ever been in a gang? What was the gang like? Was it criminal or social?

Answer: Your heroine, despite her sweet and quirky nature, was once part of a “gang” in high school. However, this wasn’t a typical gang involved in criminal activities. Instead, it was a group of self-proclaimed “Grammar Police” who roamed the school halls correcting grammatical errors and enforcing proper punctuation. This experience could be a source of humor, as she recounts her past exploits with a mix of nostalgia and embarrassment, while also showcasing her intelligence and attention to detail, skills that could prove useful in solving the mystery.

Heroine Profile:

Name: Penelope “Penny” Parsons

Occupation: Librarian

Competencies:

Penny’s occupation as a librarian provides several competencies that can be used in humorous romantic suspense:

Research Skills: Penny is a master of research, able to navigate databases and archives with ease. This skill will be invaluable in uncovering clues and delving into the background of suspects. Imagine her humorously navigating the dark web or deciphering coded messages using her knowledge of the Dewey Decimal System.

Attention to Detail: As a librarian, Penny has a keen eye for detail, noticing inconsistencies and spotting subtle clues that others might miss. This could be played for laughs as she obsesses over misplaced commas or typos in threatening notes from the villain.

Organization Skills: Penny is highly organized, able to categorize information and keep track of complex details. This can be helpful in organizing evidence and timelines in the investigation, and also be a source of humor as she color-codes clues or alphabetizes suspects.

Unexpected Knowledge: Librarians often have a wide range of knowledge due to their exposure to various books and resources. Penny could have surprising expertise in a particular area, like local history, cryptography, or even self-defense, that comes in handy during the investigation.

Animal Whisperer: Penny has a unique ability to connect with animals, which could lead to humorous situations where she gets help from unexpected creatures, like a flock of pigeons or a stray cat, to solve the mystery.

Model:

Hero and Plot Type:

Given Penny’s personality as a quirky and detail-oriented librarian, a hero who thrives in chaos and relies on intuition would create a hilarious dynamic.

Plot Type: The Investigation

Hero: Detective Jack Callahan – a rough-around-the-edges, instinctive detective with a disregard for rules and a penchant for jumping to conclusions. He’s the opposite of Penny in every way, creating a classic “opposites attract” scenario.

Conflict Setup:

Penny stumbles upon a dead body in the library, making her a key witness in the investigation. Detective Callahan, assigned to the case, immediately clashes with Penny’s methodical and meticulous nature. He finds her attention to detail and insistence on following procedures frustrating, while she’s annoyed by his impulsiveness and disregard for the rules.

Here are some ways Jack can annoy Penny:

Disrupting her organized world: Jack constantly messes up her perfectly organized crime scene, leaving coffee cups on her meticulously arranged evidence or rearranging her carefully categorized notes.

Ignoring her insights: He dismisses her observations and deductions, considering them irrelevant or “librarian talk,” only to later realize she was right all along.

Breaking library rules: He talks loudly on his phone, eats messy snacks, and disregards the “silence please” signs, much to Penny’s exasperation.

Teasing her about her quirks: He pokes fun at her literal interpretations of things and her obsession with grammar, creating witty banter and humorous exchanges.

This dynamic between the meticulous librarian and the impulsive detective will create a humorous and engaging romantic suspense, as they learn to work together, appreciate each other’s strengths, and eventually fall in love amidst the chaos of the investigation.

User: Look through Dangerous Love and design a diabolical villain likely to stymie Jack and place Penny in danger, even though she doesn’t believe she’s in danger. Make Jack frustrated as he just knows this villain is bad but Penny can’t recognize it.

Model:

Diabolical Villain:

Villain: Arthur Blackwood – A charming and charismatic philanthropist who is a major donor to the library and a well-respected member of the community. He appears to be a kind and generous benefactor, but beneath the surface lies a dark secret and a twisted motive.

Villain’s Connection to Penny: Arthur has taken a special interest in Penny, impressed by her intelligence and dedication. He showers her with compliments and gifts, positioning himself as a mentor and friend. Penny, oblivious to his true intentions, is flattered by his attention and sees him as a harmless admirer.

Jack’s Suspicions: Detective Callahan, with his intuitive nature and experience dealing with criminals, senses something is off about Arthur. He finds Arthur’s charm superficial and his motives suspicious. However, without concrete evidence, he is unable to convince Penny of the danger she’s in.

Making it Diabolical:
